================================================================================
1. PROJECT IDENTITY
================================================================================
- Project Name: Zootopia Club
- Package Manifest Name: `react-example` in `package.json` (legacy package name; not the product name).
- Purpose: AI-assisted science education platform with document analysis, quiz generation, study tools, chatbot flows, image/infographic generation, live voice tooling, admin governance, billing, and communication systems.
- Current Status: Active development. The repo supports both integrated local development and split production deployments.
- Current Architecture Style: React SPA frontend plus Express/TypeScript backend, backed by Firebase Auth/Firestore/Storage, with server-authoritative AI execution, billing, entitlements, admin governance, and owner-scoped document-runtime orchestration.
- Runtime Shape:
  - Local development is a single integrated process through `server.ts`, which mounts Vite middleware and serves the React app.
  - Production-capable deployments can split static frontend hosting from the API/backend runtime.
- Ledger Snapshot Refreshed: 2026-03-29
- Verified Against: `package.json`, `package-lock.json`, `vite.config.ts`, `server.ts`, `firebase.json`, `netlify.toml`, `cloudbuild.yaml`, `Dockerfile`, `.env.example`, `cloudrun.env`, `deployment/runtime-manifest.json`, `firestore.rules`, `storage.rules`, `src/`, `server/`, and `tests/`.

2. DEPENDENCY / RUNTIME AUDIT
================================================================================
- Runtime Baselines:
  - Node.js engine: `22.x` (`package.json`)
  - Python runtime contract: `3.11` (`deployment/runtime-manifest.json`)
  - Backend entry: `server.ts`
  - Frontend output: `dist`
- Exact installed versions verified from `package-lock.json`:
  - Frontend core: React `19.2.4`, React DOM `19.2.4`, React Router DOM `7.13.1`, Vite `6.4.1`, TypeScript `5.8.3`
  - Styling / UI: Tailwind CSS `4.2.2`, `@tailwindcss/vite` `4.2.2`, motion `12.38.0`, lucide-react `0.546.0`, react-hot-toast `2.6.0`, recharts `3.8.0`
  - Firebase / auth / data: firebase `12.11.0`, firebase-admin `13.7.0`, `@react-oauth/google` `0.13.4`
  - Backend / runtime: Express `4.22.1`, tsx `4.21.0`, dotenv `17.2.3`, redis `4.7.1`, better-sqlite3 `12.8.0`, nodemailer `8.0.3`
  - AI / provider SDKs: `@google/genai` `1.46.0`
  - Document / export tooling: pdfjs-dist `5.5.207`, mammoth `1.12.0`, xlsx `0.18.5`, docx `9.6.1`, jspdf `4.2.1`, jspdf-autotable `5.0.7`, html2canvas `1.4.1`, file-saver `2.0.5`

- Versioning Note:
  - `package.json` still declares broader requested ranges such as React `^19.0.0`, Vite `^6.2.0`, Firebase `^12.10.0`, and Express `^4.21.2`.
  - The exact versions above are the current installed repo state and should be treated as the most precise ledger source unless the lockfile changes.

================================================================================
3. CURRENT ARCHITECTURE & OWNERSHIP SEPARATION
================================================================================
- Frontend-authoritative code:
  - `src/` owns the React SPA, route shell, providers, tool UIs, feature modules, shared frontend services, and browser runtime adaptation.
  - `src/features/*` is the canonical home for isolated tool modules.
  - `src/components/`, `src/pages/`, and `src/hooks/` still contain both shared primitives and deliberate compatibility wrappers for older import paths.
- Backend-authoritative code:
  - `server.ts` and `server/` own auth/session validation, AI execution, billing, entitlements, admin APIs, document intake/extraction/artifact authority, monitoring, security headers, and deployment-aware runtime behavior.
  - `server/documentRuntime/` is the canonical document processing and artifact authority layer.
- Shared / cross-runtime contracts:
  - `src/config/runtime.ts` mirrors deployment target behavior on the frontend.
  - `server/runtimeConfig.ts` is the backend runtime/deploy-target authority.
  - `src/upload/documentFilePolicy.ts` is the shared upload contract used by browser and backend flows.
  - `src/types/`, `src/constants/`, and selected `src/services/*` modules provide cross-feature contracts.
- Configuration / deployment layer:
  - Root config files such as `firebase.json`, `netlify.toml`, `cloudbuild.yaml`, `Dockerfile`, `render.yaml`, `railway.toml`, `fly.toml`, `vercel.json`, and `deployment/runtime-manifest.json` define hosting/runtime behavior rather than app logic.
- Sensitive ownership exceptions:
  - `src/services/billing/paymentProviderAbstraction.ts` lives under `src/` but is explicitly backend-oriented and should be treated as server-side payment contract logic.
  - `src/services/geminiService.ts` still exists, but core AI authority has shifted toward `src/ai/services/aiExecutor.ts` plus backend execution routes.
- Current architecture direction:
  - Feature-first frontend isolation is real but incomplete. Core tool routes are mostly under `src/features/*`, while some legacy page surfaces still live under `src/pages/` or wrapper files.
  - `DocumentContext` is a frontend mirror and workspace convenience layer, not the sole backend source of truth for uploaded-document prompt context.

================================================================================
4. CONFIGURATION, ENVIRONMENT, AND DEPLOYMENT FILES
================================================================================
- Core build/runtime files:
  - `package.json`: scripts, dependency ranges, Node engine, deployment verification commands.
  - `package-lock.json`: exact installed dependency graph. Use this for precise version audits.
  - `vite.config.ts`: React + Tailwind Vite config, aliasing, HMR control, build chunking, ES2022 target, and production console stripping.
  - `server.ts`: Express server entry, API route registration, auth middleware, local Vite integration, production static serving, and runtime startup logging.
  - `deployment/runtime-manifest.json`: central runtime contract for Node/Python versions, healthcheck path, build output, worker paths, and supported deployment targets.
- Environment/config files:
  - `.env.example`: canonical environment-variable template for local/dev/prod configuration.
  - `.env`: local runtime secrets and overrides. Treat as secret-bearing and environment-specific.
  - `cloudrun.env`: Cloud Run deployment environment file containing production-oriented runtime settings and secrets. High risk.
  - `.node-version`, `.nvmrc`, `.python-version`: runtime version hints for local/tooling environments.
- Firebase config:
  - `firebase.json`: Firebase Hosting config that serves `dist` and rewrites `/api/**` to Cloud Run service `zootopia-api`.
  - `.firebaserc`: Firebase project alias mapping; current default project is `zootopia2026`.
  - `firebase-applet-config.json`: frontend Firebase app configuration consumed by `src/firebase.ts`.
  - `firebase-blueprint.json`: additional Firebase blueprint/config artifact kept at repo root.
  - `firestore.rules`, `storage.rules`: active data/storage access-control policy files.
- Hosting/container config:
  - `netlify.toml`: frontend-only Netlify build/publish config. Points browser API traffic at the backend.
  - `cloudbuild.yaml`: builds and deploys the backend container to Google Cloud Run.
  - `Dockerfile`: production-capable Node 22 + Python 3.11 container build, installs Python extraction dependencies, verifies runtime contract, and starts `server.ts`.
  - `render.yaml`, `railway.toml`, `fly.toml`, `vercel.json`: alternative deployment target configs already present in the repo.
  - `Makefile`, `tools/setup-linux-server.sh`, `tools/start-linux-server.sh`, `tools/deploymentRuntime.mjs`: deployment/runtime helper tooling.

================================================================================
5. KEY RUNTIME FILES AND INTEGRATION MAP
================================================================================
- App bootstrap and routing:
  - `src/main.tsx` installs the startup guard and cross-origin API fetch bridge, then renders `<App />`.
  - `src/App.tsx` owns the provider stack, protected-route shell, preview/payment verification handling, and workspace route mounting.
  - `src/routing/workspaceRoutes.ts` is the canonical lazy route registry and preload map. Route ownership should be updated here, not scattered across feature code.
- Frontend runtime providers:
  - `src/auth/AuthContext.tsx` is the main auth/user/session/model/usage orchestration context and remains a high-coupling hotspot.
  - `src/contexts/DocumentContext.tsx` holds frontend document runtime mirror state and must stay app-global.
  - `src/notifications/NotificationContext.tsx`, `src/notifications/ToastProvider.tsx`, `src/themes/ThemeProvider.tsx`, and `src/contexts/LanguageContext.tsx` provide shell-wide concerns.
- Auth/session flow:
  - Frontend session lifecycle lives in `src/auth/session/*`, especially `sessionApi.ts`.
  - Browser calls `/api/auth/session/bootstrap`, `/api/auth/session/refresh`, and `/api/auth/session/logout`.
  - Backend authority lives in `server/authSessionService.ts` and `server/auth/*`, with Redis-backed or local fallback session coordination.
- Document upload/extraction flow:
  - `src/upload/FileUploader.tsx` and assessment/file-analysis entry points call `src/services/documentRuntimeService.ts`.
  - The browser posts `POST /api/documents/intake` with bearer auth and document metadata headers.
  - `server.ts` routes into `server/documentRuntime/documentIntakeService.ts`, which coordinates storage, extraction, artifact persistence, runtime state registration, and cleanup behavior.
  - `server/documentRuntime/documentArtifactStore.ts` and `server/documentRuntime/promptContextResolver.ts` are the core document metadata/prompt-context authority.
- AI/model flow:
  - `src/ai/models/modelRegistry.ts` is the canonical model registry.
  - `src/ai/services/aiRouter.ts` maps tool intents to AI execution plans.
  - `src/ai/services/aiExecutor.ts` handles authorization, trace stages, provider dispatch, fallback, and backend execution routing.
  - Backend execution flows through `/api/ai/authorize-model` and `/api/ai/execute`, then into `server/providerRuntime.ts`, `server/aiProviders.ts`, and `server/promptOrchestrator.ts`.
- Admin flow:
  - `src/admin/AdminPanel.tsx` is the main admin shell.
  - `src/admin/components/*` hosts governance tools such as monitoring, refunds, codes, entitlement management, communication, stored-results exploration, and fast-access account management.
  - Backend admin authority is exposed via `/api/admin/*` routes and implemented by services such as `adminAccountDirectoryService.ts`, `monitoringService.ts`, `codeService.ts`, `providerSecuritySummary.ts`, and admin route logic in `server.ts`.
- Billing/results/communication flow:
  - Billing UI starts in pages such as `src/pages/Billing.tsx`, `src/pages/Pricing.tsx`, and `src/pages/Donation.tsx`.
  - Frontend service entry points include `src/services/billing/paymentService.ts`, `src/services/generatedAssetService.ts`, `src/services/resultService.ts`, and `src/services/communicationService.ts`.
  - Backend authority for payments and payment effects lives in `server/billingService.ts`; communication/email dispatch lives in `server/communicationService.ts`.

================================================================================
6. VERIFIED PLATFORM SYSTEMS
================================================================================
- Auth / Session Architecture:
  - Firebase Auth establishes browser identity, but platform session lifecycle is additionally managed through backend session APIs and `server/authSessionService.ts`.
  - Supported auth modes are distinct: normal, fast-access, and admin.
  - Session refresh invalidation is intentionally conservative on the frontend; transient failures should not casually wipe active sessions.
  - Fast-access flows under `/api/auth/fast-access/faculty-science/*` are intentionally separate from the full-account lifecycle.
- Document Runtime / Upload / Extraction Architecture:
  - Upload policy is centralized in `src/upload/documentFilePolicy.ts`.
  - Frontend uploads stream through `src/services/documentRuntimeService.ts`.
  - Backend authority lives in `server/documentRuntime/*`, with layered responsibilities for file-type detection, extraction, OCR/native strategies, artifact storage, prompt-context assembly, cleanup, and runtime state coordination.
  - Current extraction version in `server/documentRuntime/config.ts` is `2026.03.layered-runtime-v2`.
  - The `direct_file_to_model` path exists in code but remains dormant compared with the active local-extraction pathway.
- AI / Model / Orchestration Architecture:
  - Gemini and Qwen providers are both wired.
  - Model metadata and tool capability routing are centralized in `src/ai/models/modelRegistry.ts`, `src/ai/services/aiRouter.ts`, and `src/ai/services/aiExecutor.ts`.
  - Backend execution is server-authoritative for provider credentials, usage logging, and model authorization.
  - `src/ai/services/aiExecutor.ts` still contains a deliberate frontend Gemini path for explicit user-supplied API keys; standard platform flow remains backend-managed.
  - Prompt orchestration remains cross-cutting; `server/promptOrchestrator.ts` currently acts as a backend boundary/re-export rather than a totally separate implementation.
- Admin System Architecture:
  - Admin UI remains isolated under `src/admin/`.
  - The admin shell currently covers user/admin lifecycle, fast-access accounts, monitoring, codes, refunds, donations, communications, stored results, and entitlement management.
  - Admin-sensitive backend helpers include `adminAccountDirectoryService.ts`, `providerSecuritySummary.ts`, `monitoringService.ts`, and route-level admin checks in `server.ts`.
- Billing / Payments / Entitlements Architecture:
  - Billing is backend-authoritative.
  - Providers currently represented in the frontend abstraction are Paymob, FawryPay, and EasyKash.
  - `server/billingService.ts` handles checkout creation, payment verification, refunds, webhook processing, and payment-side effects such as subscriptions and unlocks.
  - Tool/model/page unlocks and related code redemption are intentionally routed through backend entitlement and billing services.
- Communication / Notification Architecture:
  - User/admin messaging data is stored in Firestore-facing services under `src/services/communicationService.ts` and related helpers.
  - Unified email send endpoints exist under `/api/admin/email/*`, backed by `server/communicationService.ts` and Nodemailer.
  - Notification/inbox behavior spans `src/notifications/*`, Firestore collections, and `/api/notifications/*` routes.
- Results / Assets / Preview Architecture:
  - Generated asset metadata lives through `src/services/generatedAssetService.ts` and related metadata helpers, with owner-scoped content delivery via `/api/assets/:assetId/content`.
  - Result persistence and export are handled by `src/services/resultService.ts`, `src/services/resultExportService.ts`, `src/components/status/*`, and `src/pages/DetachedResultPreviewPage.tsx`.

7. FEATURE / TOOL INVENTORY
================================================================================
- Assessment dashboard and quiz flow:

  - Owns the `/generate` assessment landing experience, upload-first workflow, quiz generation UI, and analysis launch handoff.
- File analysis workspace:
  - `src/features/file-analysis/`
  - Owns dedicated document analysis route/page behavior and normalized analysis result presentation.
- Chatbot:
  - `src/features/chatbot/`
  - Chat UI can consume current document context and model selection.
- Image generation:
  - `src/features/image-generator/`
  - Generates images, stores generated assets, and connects into the editor/results flows.
- Infographic generation:
  - `src/features/infographic-generator/`
  - Handles infographic prompt/data generation, preview/export, and optional image generation helpers.
- Study tools:
  - `src/features/study-tools/`
  - Hosts summary/flashcard/mind-map/concept/note-style workflows with per-tool prompt orchestration.
- Live voice:
  - `src/features/live-voice/`
  - Voice-session UI and transcript/export flows.
- Video generation:
  - `src/features/video-generator/`
  - Current page exists, but real backend generation is intentionally not fully enabled; the code prefers an honest "not live" state over fake success behavior.
- Admin workspace:
  - `src/admin/`
  - Separate admin shell with monitoring, codes, communications, refunds, donations, accounts, entitlements, and stored-result tooling.

  - `src/components/UserHistory.tsx`

================================================================================
8. SENSITIVE / HIGH-RISK FILES AND DO-NOT-CHANGE-CASUALLY AREAS
================================================================================
- `server.ts`
  - Central backend entrypoint. Route wiring, CORS, auth middleware, AI execution, document runtime, billing, admin routes, local Vite integration, and production static serving all converge here.
- `src/auth/AuthContext.tsx`
  - Large, high-coupling frontend auth/user/session/model orchestration file. Casual refactors can break login, session refresh, usage state, and admin/fast-access behavior simultaneously.
- `server/authSessionService.ts` and `server/auth/*`
  - Backend session authority. Changes here directly affect session expiry, auth mode separation, invalidation, and document-runtime scoping.
- `server/documentRuntime/*`
  - Treat as backend-authoritative document ingestion/extraction/storage context. In particular: `documentIntakeService.ts`, `documentArtifactStore.ts`, `promptContextResolver.ts`, `runtimeStateService.ts`, and `config.ts`.
- `src/ai/models/modelRegistry.ts` and `src/ai/services/aiExecutor.ts`
  - Registry and execution center for model availability, routing, fallback, authorization, and provider dispatch behavior.
- `server/billingService.ts` plus entitlement services
  - Backend-authoritative payment side effects, unlock grants, refunds, and verification behavior.
- `src/services/billing/paymentProviderAbstraction.ts`
  - Path is misleading. It is backend-sensitive payment contract logic and should not be treated like ordinary browser-only code.
- `firestore.rules` and `storage.rules`
  - Security-critical access-control policy. Do not make convenience edits here without tracing user/admin/owner implications.
- `.env`, `cloudrun.env`, `serviceAccountKey.json`
  - Secret-bearing files. `cloudrun.env` and `serviceAccountKey.json` are especially sensitive and should not be exposed, rewritten casually, or copied into docs/logs.
- `runtime/document-workspaces/`
  - Contains live local document-runtime workspaces and potentially user/admin file artifacts. Do not treat as a harmless scratch folder.
- Compatibility wrappers under `src/components/`, `src/pages/AnalysisPage.tsx`, and `src/hooks/useDocumentAnalysisWorkspace.ts`
  - They may look redundant, but they still protect import compatibility during the feature-first migration.

================================================================================
9. CURRENT DEPLOYMENT TARGETS AND RUNTIME RELATIONSHIPS
================================================================================
- Local integrated runtime:
  - `npm run dev` and `npm run start` both execute `tsx server.ts`.
  - In non-production, `server.ts` mounts Vite middleware and serves both API and SPA from the same process.
  - `.env` and `.env.example` define local runtime variables; local document extraction can use the Python virtual environment.
- Firebase Hosting + Cloud Run:
  - `firebase.json` serves the built SPA from `dist`.
  - `/api/**` is rewritten to Cloud Run service `zootopia-api` in `us-central1`.
  - `cloudbuild.yaml` and `Dockerfile` define the backend container build/deploy path used by Cloud Run.
- Netlify + backend API split:
  - `netlify.toml` is explicitly frontend-only.
  - Browser API traffic is redirected via `VITE_API_BASE_URL`, with `src/config/runtime.ts` rewriting relative `/api/*` requests when the frontend is cross-origin from the API.
- Vercel:
  - `vercel.json` is a static/frontend deployment config for the built Vite app. It does not replace the backend API runtime.
- Render / Railway / Fly / Docker / generic Linux:
  - `render.yaml`, `railway.toml`, `fly.toml`, `Dockerfile`, and helper scripts under `tools/` provide alternative backend-capable deployment paths already scaffolded in the repo.
- Central deployment contract:
  - `deployment/runtime-manifest.json` is the best single-file summary of supported runtime targets and should stay aligned with deployment configs and the Docker build.

================================================================================
10. FUTURE DEVELOPER / AGENT GUIDANCE
================================================================================
- Put new tool-specific UI/state/prompt-shaping code inside `src/features/<tool>/` first. Do not expand legacy wrapper files unless the change is explicitly about compatibility.
- Keep backend authority on the backend:
  - auth/session validation
  - billing/payment effects
  - entitlements/unlocks
  - provider credentials and AI execution authority
  - owner-scoped document artifacts and prompt-context resolution
- When changing deployment behavior, review both `src/config/runtime.ts` and `server/runtimeConfig.ts` together.
- Do not casually remove compatibility bridge files. Verify the import graph first.
- Treat `AuthContext.tsx`, `server.ts`, model registry/executor files, billing services, and document-runtime services as staged-refactor territory, not opportunistic cleanup targets.
- `DocumentProvider` must remain app-global unless the backend document-runtime model is redesigned. Uploaded files are intentionally shared resources across tools.
- Keep admin code isolated under `src/admin/` and admin backend routes/services. Do not mix it into normal-user feature folders.
- Preserve honest product state:
  - The current video generator is intentionally not pretending to have a full live backend.
  - Dormant codepaths such as direct file-to-model document dispatch should remain clearly marked until explicitly activated end-to-end.
- Maintain deployment alignment:
  - Firebase Hosting rewrite target names must stay aligned with the Cloud Run service name.
  - Environment files, runtime manifest, and container/runtime scripts should be updated together.
- Continue the feature-first migration carefully:
  - Remaining route-heavy surfaces such as image editor, results library, projects, billing/account pages, and user history are still good candidates for future ownership cleanup.
  - Refactoring `AuthContext.tsx` into smaller context boundaries remains a real maintainability opportunity, but it should be planned, not improvised.

12. CHANGE LOG / MODIFICATION HISTORY
- 2026-03-22: Added backend-authoritative admin lifecycle management for Faculty fast-access accounts.
  - Added dedicated admin endpoints in `server.ts` for temporary account management: list/filter (`GET /api/admin/fast-access/accounts`), create by phone (`POST /api/admin/fast-access/accounts`), status updates (`POST /api/admin/fast-access/accounts/:userId/status`), and safe remove/delete (`DELETE /api/admin/fast-access/accounts/:userId`).
  - Added `FastAccessAccountsManager` in `src/admin/components/FastAccessAccountsManager.tsx` and integrated it into `src/admin/AdminPanel.tsx` as a dedicated admin view.
  - Preserved strict separation from full-user lifecycle by hard guards that reject operations on non-fast-access accounts and by architecture comments warning against collapsing temporary scope into normal user semantics.
  - Updated integrated users table credit display so temporary accounts show `fastAccessCredits` instead of normal `credits`.
  - Unified conversion prompt copy across temporary journey screens using shared constant `FACULTY_FAST_ACCESS_CONVERSION_PROMPT` in `src/constants/fastAccessPolicy.ts`, consumed by `src/components/MainLayout.tsx`, `src/pages/Account.tsx`, and `src/components/FastAccessLockedState.tsx`.
  - Reason: Give admins safe, explicit control over temporary Faculty accounts while keeping backend authorization authoritative and preserving temporary/full-account separation.
- 2026-03-22: Enhanced Faculty fast-access conversion UX and audit filtering shortcuts.

- 2026-03-22: Architecture analysis pass for unified entitlement, unlock, billing, and credits hardening (analysis-only phase).
  - Scope: Mapped current lock/unlock and charging boundaries across UI, backend APIs, code issuance, gift/redeem flows, notification dispatch, and result persistence.
  - Verified security boundaries:
    - Backend authority for temporary Faculty fast-access tool allowlist and success-only credit deduction in `/api/ai/execute`.
    - Admin middleware protection for privileged code/billing/user routes.
  - Key architecture risks identified:
    - Mixed authority paths (frontend direct Firestore writes + backend API flows) for unlock and request processing.
    - Divergent code systems (`unlockCodes`, `issuedCodes`, `secretCodes`, `giftCodes`) with overlapping responsibilities and inconsistent verification semantics.
    - Secret-code verification currently grants credits regardless of purpose, creating entitlement leakage risk.
    - Legacy client-side credit deduction still used in multiple non-fast-access tools without consistent post-success backend idempotency.
  - Separation plan ratified (no implementation yet):
    - Introduce backend-owned entitlement ledger for per-tool unlock state.
    - Keep billing transactions, unlock entitlements, and operational credit balances as distinct bounded contexts.
    - Route all unlock purchases/redeems through backend APIs with idempotent event writes.
    - Keep notifications as projection side-effects of entitlement/billing events, not as state authority.
  - Planned implementation phases (next):
    1) Canonical data contracts and ownership boundaries.
    2) Backend entitlement APIs + idempotent unlock events + admin revoke flows.
    3) Billing integration for per-tool 200 EGP unlock path.
    4) UI lock modal refactor to backend-driven state.
    5) Notification/inbox projection wiring and audit dashboards.
    6) Migration/cleanup of legacy frontend-write unlock and code paths.
  - Reason: Establish a production-safe hardening roadmap before code changes to prevent coupling regressions and entitlement bypasses.
- 2026-03-22: Phase 1A implemented - canonical backend contract/types module plus validation scaffolding (non-enforcing).
  - Affected files: `/server/entitlementContracts.ts`, `/server.ts`.
  - Added canonical backend contracts for entitlement and unlock ecosystem:
    - `CANONICAL_UNLOCK_ELIGIBLE_TOOL_IDS` restricted to `infographic`, `quiz`, `analyze`.
    - `CANONICAL_UNLOCK_PRICE_EGP` set to `200`.
    - Canonical types/interfaces for entitlement records, unlock purchase intents, gift-code issuance input, and operational credit receipts.
  - Added validation helpers and scaffolding utilities:
    - `validateUnlockCodePolicy`, `validateGiftCodeIssueInput`, `validateUnlockPurchaseIntent`, `validateOperationalCreditReceipt`, and `collectContractWarnings`.
  - Integrated validation scaffolding into backend routes without behavior switches:
    - Added advisory contract checks/logging to `/api/admin/generate-code`, `/api/admin/gift-codes`, and `/api/ai/execute`.
    - Violations are currently diagnostic warnings (non-blocking) to preserve current UX/runtime behavior.
  - Reason: Establish canonical backend contract boundaries first, with zero UI behavior change and no lock-enforcement switch in this phase.
- 2026-03-22: Implemented premium unlock-entry flow and backend-authoritative tool unlock redemption/payment path.
  - Affected files: `/src/components/Sidebar.tsx`, `/src/components/ProtectedRoute.tsx`, `/server.ts`, `/server/billingService.ts`, `/src/admin/components/CodeManager.tsx`.
  - Added sidebar unlock-entry modal for fast-access eligible tools with two options:
    - admin-issued unlock code redemption
    - secure paid unlock checkout at canonical `200 EGP`
  - Added backend endpoint `POST /api/unlocks/redeem-tool-code`:
    - verifies token-authenticated user
    - redeems via `issuedCodes` (`purpose=tool-unlock`) with code-status/expiry/usage enforcement
    - enforces canonical eligible tool IDs and code target-tool compatibility
    - updates user entitlements (`unlockedTools`, `unlockedPages`) server-side
  - Added backend endpoint `POST /api/billing/create-tool-unlock-checkout`:
    - validates canonical eligible tool IDs only
    - creates checkout using existing billing provider flow
    - persists transaction intent as `type=tool_unlock` for verification-time entitlement grant
  - Enhanced billing verification logic in `billingService.verifyPayment`:
    - when `transaction.type === tool_unlock` and payment succeeds, grants entitlements to the correct tool/page.
  - Hardened admin unlock issuance UX in `CodeManager`:
    - added target-tool selection, usage mode, optional max uses, expiry/never-expires policy, optional recipient email
    - generates `tool-unlock` codes through existing admin API and auto-activates status
    - keeps pause/revoke controls intact for revocation workflow compatibility.
  - Reason: enforce backend authority for unlock validity/redeem lifecycle while providing a premium, short unlock entry experience for the eligible tool surface.
- 2026-03-22: Hardened per-tool payment unlock authority, admin entitlement governance, and centralized unlock-code paths.
  - Affected files: `/server.ts`, `/server/toolEntitlementService.ts`, `/server/billingService.ts`, `/src/admin/components/ToolEntitlementsManager.tsx`, `/src/admin/AdminPanel.tsx`, `/src/services/accessControl/codeService.ts`, `/src/auth/hooks/useRequestManagement.ts`, `/src/components/ModelSelector.tsx`, `/src/components/PageLock.tsx`, `/src/pages/Billing.tsx`, `/src/services/toolUnlockErrorMap.ts`, `/tests/toolUnlockErrorMap.test.ts`, `/tests/toolUnlockEntitlementGrant.test.ts`, `/package.json`.
  - Payment unlock hardening:
    - Enforced canonical per-tool unlock amount at `200 EGP` through existing billing architecture (`create-tool-unlock-checkout`).
    - Added backend-authoritative, idempotent payment verification grant path in `/api/billing/verify-payment` with transaction markers to prevent replay grants.
    - Ensured failed/abandoned payments do not grant entitlements because grant executes only on verified `success` status.
  - Backend entitlement authority:

- 2026-03-22: Payment system hardening architecture audit (analysis-only phase, no behavior changes).
  - Scope audited end-to-end:
    - Payment initiation routes and UI entrypoints (`/api/billing/create-subscription`, `/api/billing/create-donation`, `/api/billing/create-tool-unlock-checkout`, Pricing/Donation/Sidebar flows).
    - Payment confirmation routes and callback UX (`/api/billing/verify-payment`, Billing/Donation/App callback handling).
    - Provider integration layer (Paymob primary adapter, provider registry/default selection, webhook and refund adapter contracts).
    - Business effects after payment (subscription plan updates, tool entitlement grants, donation handling, refund reversals).
    - Notification/email/admin observability/payment-history/refund control touchpoints.
  - Exact files inspected in this analysis phase:
    - `/package.json`, `/server.ts`, `/server/billingService.ts`, `/server/communicationService.ts`, `/server/diagnostics.ts`, `/.env.example`, `/firestore.rules`.
    - `/src/types/billing.ts`, `/src/services/billing/paymentProviderAbstraction.ts`, `/src/services/billing/paymentService.ts`, `/src/services/billing/adapters/paymobAdapter.ts`, `/src/services/billing/adapters/fawryPayAdapter.ts`, `/src/services/billing/adapters/easyKashAdapter.ts`.
    - `/src/pages/Pricing.tsx`, `/src/pages/Billing.tsx`, `/src/pages/Donation.tsx`, `/src/App.tsx`, `/src/admin/components/RefundsView.tsx`, `/src/utils/validators.ts`.
  - Confirmed architecture strengths preserved:
    - Provider abstraction and registry are in place with Paymob as active default.
    - Backend retains payment authority for status mutation and post-payment state transitions.
    - Tool unlock payment grants are backend-authoritative and include idempotent replay guards at verification layer.
    - Refund pipeline exists with duplicate-refund protection and provider adapter delegation.
  - High-risk/fragile areas identified for hardening:
    - `/api/billing/create-subscription` and `/api/billing/verify-payment` are currently unauthenticated routes.
    - Session identifiers are predictable (`SUB-*`/`DON-*`) and verification trust depends heavily on callback flow discipline.
    - Webhook route uses provider-param multiplexing with weak header/signature normalization and fail-open behavior in some adapters.
    - User billing history is currently static UI mock data rather than transaction-backed records.
    - Admin payment tooling currently focuses on refunds; transaction-level observability/search/filter/audit endpoints are incomplete.
    - Payment lifecycle notifications/emails are uneven (tool unlock has internal notifications; subscription/donation/refund lifecycle messaging is not consistently projected).
    - Diagnostics are present but not fully trace-correlated across route -> provider -> webhook -> business effect chain.
  - Safe phased hardening plan ratified (implementation next phase):
    1) Route authority hardening (auth/admin middleware + ownership checks + strict request validation).
    2) Verification trust hardening (session ownership binding, idempotency keys, explicit status transition guards).
    3) Webhook hardening (provider-specific signature extraction, strict verification policy, replay protection).
    4) Transaction visibility APIs (user payment history + admin transaction audit endpoints with filters/pagination).
    5) Lifecycle projection completion (consistent notification/inbox/email events for subscription/donation/refund outcomes).
    6) Diagnostics/monitoring upgrades (trace propagation, structured billing events, failure taxonomy, alertable metrics).
    7) Refund governance upgrades (status machine normalization, partial/full refund controls, communication hooks, audit metadata).
  - Preservation guarantee:
    - No runtime/payment behavior was modified in this phase.
    - Existing provider abstraction, billing service boundaries, and entitlement separation contracts remain intact.

- 2026-03-23: Fast-access student admin-management hardening for edit controls, suspend messaging, and re-entry safety.
  - Affected files: `/server.ts`, `/src/admin/components/FastAccessAccountsManager.tsx`, `/src/auth/AccountStatus.tsx`, `/src/auth/hooks/useAuthActions.ts`, `/src/utils.ts`.
  - Backend authority hardening:

You are working on an EXISTING production-style project called Zootopia Club.

ROLE
You are a careful senior software engineer working on a live, evolving, production-style platform.
Your job is to make precise, minimal, safe, well-reasoned, backward-compatible improvements.
You must extend and harden the current architecture, not fight it, replace it, or redesign it unnecessarily.

CRITICAL NON-NEGOTIABLE RULES
- Do NOT rebuild files from scratch unless explicitly requested.
- Do NOT break existing core behavior.
- Do NOT rename public APIs, component contracts, service interfaces, routes, collection names, database field names, or shared state shape unless absolutely necessary and clearly documented.
- Do NOT remove defensive helpers, normalization layers, guards, validation layers, fallback logic, compatibility code, or inline architectural comments that were intentionally added.
- Always build ON TOP OF the current file structure and logic, not against it.
- Preserve compatibility with the rest of the project.
- Any refactor must be incremental, safe, and backward-compatible.
- Do NOT modify anything outside the requested scope.
- Do NOT hallucinate files, dependencies, architecture, routes, components, schemas, hooks, services, or behaviors.
- Verify everything against the real codebase before acting.
- Use 2026 best practices.
- Always prefer precision over speed.
- Always prefer evidence over assumptions.
- Always prefer minimal safe edits over broad rewrites.

PROJECT CONTEXT
- Project: Zootopia Club
- Type: AI-powered science education platform
- Frontend: React + TypeScript + Tailwind
- Backend: Express + Firebase Admin + Firestore
- Auth: Firebase Auth (Email/Password + Google)
- Admin features: communication center, inbox, moderation, codes, billing, refunds, monitoring
- Messaging: internal inbox, notifications, popup/toast logic, email system
- Codes: gift codes, secrets access, model unlock, tool unlock, chat unlock
- Billing: payment providers and refund flows
- Data layer: Firestore collections with admin/user separation
- Architecture goal: modular, readable, scalable, future-ready, strongly validated

GLOBAL PRIORITIES
1. Preserve all existing working functionality.
2. Never rebuild from scratch unless explicitly requested.
3. Never perform broad refactors unless explicitly requested.
4. Never modify unrelated areas.
5. Make the smallest possible change that fully solves the requested task.
6. Maintain architectural consistency with the current codebase.
7. Preserve backward compatibility unless explicitly told otherwise.
8. Keep the code modular, readable, validated, and resilient.
9. Respect the existing architecture, file structure, and naming.
10. Keep all updates documented in the project ledger.

MANDATORY ANALYSIS BEFORE ANY EDIT
Before writing or changing any code, you must:
1. Analyze the current codebase carefully.
2. Read all relevant files fully, not just one file.
3. Trace dependencies, imports, exports, shared types, hooks, contexts, state flows, services, routes, schemas, parsers, utilities, and UI usage.
4. Identify exactly what belongs to frontend and what belongs to backend.
5. Understand the data flow end-to-end before editing.
6. Detect sensitive, central, or tightly coupled files before touching them.
7. Check whether the requested change affects:
   - UI components
   - state management
   - hooks and contexts
   - services
   - API endpoints
   - database schemas / Firestore documents
   - authentication / authorization
   - admin-only logic
   - localization
   - responsiveness
   - dark mode
   - validation
   - normalization
   - error handling
   - notifications / toasts / inbox messaging
8. Write a short internal impact assessment before making any change.
9. Do not start editing until the code relationships are understood.

CHANGE CONTROL RULES
1. Do not change any file unless the request truly requires it.
2. Do not rename files, variables, functions, props, routes, collections, or folders unless explicitly required.
3. Do not delete existing logic unless it is directly part of the requested task.
4. Do not â€œclean upâ€‌ unrelated code.
5. Do not introduce â€œnice to haveâ€‌ changes unless explicitly asked.
6. Do not alter styling, layout, wording, architecture, behavior, or data flow outside the requested scope.
7. Do not replace current project patterns with your personal preferred patterns unless requested.
8. Respect the current project structure and conventions.
9. If a better architecture is needed, implement it progressively without breaking old usage.
10. If a file contains compatibility logic, preserve it unless there is a direct, verified reason to adjust it safely.

GLOBAL FILE UPDATE POLICY
1. Preserve the fileâ€™s public contract.
2. Preserve existing working flows unless they are clearly fragile or broken and directly relevant to the requested task.
3. Improve validation, normalization, comments, readability, maintainability, and resilience.
4. Add helper functions instead of duplicating logic.

10. If a better architecture is needed, implement it progressively without breaking old usage.
11. Always update ZOOTOPIA_PROJECT_LEDGER.txt after every meaningful change.

FRONTEND / BACKEND SEPARATION
You must strictly separate frontend and backend concerns.
Never mix client logic with server logic.

Frontend responsibilities:
- React components
- UI rendering
- client-side state
- hooks
- forms
- responsive layout
- presentational logic
- frontend service calls
- local validation
- UX feedback

Backend responsibilities:
- API routes
- server-side validation
- business logic
- provider orchestration
- secure token / secret handling
- Firestore writes requiring trust
- privileged admin logic
- billing/refund/security-sensitive flows
- server-only integrations
- monitoring / audit-safe logic

Rules:
1. Never place backend logic inside frontend components.
2. Never expose secrets, tokens, admin logic, private orchestration, or privileged behavior to the frontend.
3. Never duplicate backend business logic in the frontend unless explicitly required for UX.
4. If a change touches both frontend and backend, update them in a coordinated, compatibility-safe way.
5. If schemas or payload contracts change, update all dependent layers carefully and minimally.

- small mobile
- mobile

- laptop
- desktop
- ultra-wide screens

UI rules:

REACT FILE RULES

- Preserve component contracts.

- Add normalization layers before filtering/rendering external data.
- Keep state grouped logically.

BACKEND FILE RULES

- Add validation where needed.

- Prefer centralized constants/helpers over raw duplicated strings.
- Improve logging without unexpectedly changing external behavior.

- Keep admin-only and privileged logic hardened.

FIRESTORE / STATE / AUTH RULES
- Never trust raw documents blindly.
- Normalize legacy, partial, or inconsistent data.

- Keep Google-authenticated users and legacy Firestore docs supported.

DEPRECATED / OUTDATED PACKAGE RULE

- UI/component libraries

- theme libraries
- browser-dependent utilities

Do not introduce a library that may break rendering, hydration, state behavior, hooks behavior, or browser compatibility for the current React version.

INSTALL / UPGRADE / REPLACEMENT SAFETY
If a package must be installed, updated, or replaced:
- do it minimally
- keep versions compatible with the project
- avoid unnecessary package churn
- avoid introducing overlapping duplicate libraries
- avoid replacing strong existing libraries without strong reason
- verify peer dependencies
- verify React compatibility
- verify TypeScript compatibility where relevant
- verify browser/runtime implications
- verify build compatibility with the current bundler/tooling

LOCKFILE CONSISTENCY RULE
If dependencies change, ensure consistency between:
- `package.json`
- `package-lock.json`

Do not leave dependency declarations inconsistent.
Do not add imports to code for packages that are not properly declared and installed.
Do not leave stale package references behind.

FRONTEND LIBRARY CAUTION RULE
Pay special attention to libraries that directly affect the browser UI/runtime.
These libraries must be checked with extra care to avoid:
- runtime crashes
- hydration/rendering mismatches
- broken hooks behavior
- browser API incompatibilities
- build failures
- CSS conflicts
- UI glitches
- bundle instability

If there is uncertainty, verify using official 2026 docs before proceeding.

OUTPUT REQUIREMENT FOR EVERY TASK
Before implementation, provide a short dependency audit section that includes:
1. current React version detected
2. relevant library versions detected
3. missing packages used by the code, if any
4. deprecated/outdated/risky packages, if any
5. whether each required library is:
   - already valid
   - needs installation
   - needs upgrade
   - needs replacement
6. why any package change is necessary
7. confirmation that the proposed dependency set is compatible with the projectâ€™s React version

DO NOT DO THESE THINGS
- Do not assume a package is installed just because it is imported.
- Do not assume a package is React-compatible without verification.
- Do not add a package without checking official docs first.
- Do not replace libraries casually.
- Do not update packages blindly.
- Do not ignore peer dependency constraints.
- Do not ignore `package-lock.json`.
- Do not rely on unofficial guesses when compatibility is unclear.

FINAL RULE
Always verify dependencies first.
Always verify React compatibility first.
Always verify official 2026 documentation first.
Always keep `package.json`, `package-lock.json`, and code imports aligned.
Always prefer safe, compatible, officially-supported dependency decisions.

  - Type/lint diagnostics reported no errors in modified files after implementation.

    - failed asset/session/version loads exit into a visible retry state instead of an endless implicit wait.
  - Hardened `/src/pages/Settings.tsx` and `/src/pages/Account.tsx` so user-profile-dependent routes no longer render `null`/empty data during auth hydration; they now show a visible profile-restore state and a retry path when the user scope cannot be resolved.
  - Fixed `/src/components/Inbox.tsx` deadlock behavior by removing the one-shot `auth.currentUser` early return that could leave `loading=true` forever when the component mounted before auth had fully hydrated.
- Verification:
  - `npm run build` completed successfully on 2026-03-25 after these changes.
  - Secondary protected routes now build into dedicated chunks (`Pricing`, `Billing`, `Account`, `Settings`, `ResultsLibraryPage`, `ImageEditorPage`) and are included in the post-auth preload strategy instead of remaining cold-only imports.
  - Live protected-route rendering verification in headless Chrome remains limited in this environment because there is no authenticated browser session to enter the protected workspace routes directly, but the dev/runtime integration and production build both remained intact after the refactor.
- Added:
  - Shared timeout-budget constants for the AI pipeline.
  - Explicit client fetch timeout for backend AI execution.
  - Explicit provider execution timeout on the server adapters.
  - Slightly larger file-preparation timeout for document handoff.
  - Timeout-specific guard that stops automatic fallback retry after a timeout.
- Removed:
  - Unaligned `600000ms` shared service timeout ceiling.
  - Duplicate Dashboard analysis timeout layer that could fail independently from the shared AI service budget.
- Risks / Dependencies:
  - The timeout ceiling now depends on `/src/ai/config/timeoutBudgets.ts` remaining the single source of truth; future ad-hoc hardcoded timeouts in tool components would reintroduce drift.
  - Gemini SDK calls are bounded with promise timeouts rather than transport-level aborts because that SDK path is not currently wired for a narrow-scope abort-signal refactor.
  - Timeout-triggered fallback is now intentionally suppressed to keep a single user action near the 5-minute ceiling; non-timeout failures can still use the existing fallback path.

- Summary: Replaced the legacy drift-prone model catalog with a verified canonical registry, made tool model selection fully isolated per tool, moved live provider credential/endpoint resolution to the backend env runtime, and hardened provider/model routing so canonical model IDs now remain authoritative from selector through execution.
- Reason: The previous system mixed global model preference state with tool-scoped state, allowed client-owned provider config to influence live execution, and contained a very large registry with inconsistent model/runtime metadata. This pass was intended to preserve the working AI flows while making model ordering, provider routing, and env-backed execution deterministic and auditable.
- Technical Details:
  - Replaced the oversized mixed-quality registry in `/src/ai/models/modelRegistry.ts` with a curated canonical registry of verified production-relevant models and compatibility-safe aliases.
  - Added canonical registry fields required for runtime safety and admin observability:
    - `sortOrder`
    - `supportedTools`
    - structured `capabilities`
    - `supportsVision`
    - `supportsStreaming`
    - `envKeyName`
    - `baseUrlResolver`
    - `supportedRegions`
    - `adminNotes`
    - `legacyAliases`
  - Preserved backward compatibility by continuing to export `MODEL_REGISTRY`, `getModelByAnyId`, and `toCanonicalModelId`, but those helpers now normalize legacy IDs onto the canonical registry instead of trusting raw labels or stale aliases.
  - Canonicalized the priority/order contract so compatible selectors now surface:
    - `Gemini Flash` first
    - `Qwen 3.5 Plus` second
    - remaining compatible models afterward in registry order
  - Added `/src/ai/toolModelSelection.ts` as the pure selection-state engine and refactored `/src/hooks/useToolScopedModelSelection.ts` to rely on it for:
    - tool-specific localStorage keys,
    - initial compatibility-safe resolution,
    - contamination-safe re-selection fallback.
  - Removed the live generation toolsâ€™ dependence on the global selected-model fallback when initializing their local selectors (`AssessmentStudio`, `Chatbot`, `StudyTools`, `ImageGenerator`, `InfographicGenerator`, `VideoGenerator`, and Dashboard document analysis).
  - Updated `/src/components/ModelSelector.tsx` to sort compatible models using canonical registry order instead of relying on legacy array order or ad-hoc filter order.
  - Added `/server/providerRuntime.ts` as the server-authoritative provider runtime resolver:
    - Gemini resolves `GEMINI_API_KEY` from env.
    - Qwen resolves `DASHSCOPE_API_KEY` first, with `QWEN_API_KEY` kept as a legacy alias only.
    - Qwen official region/base URL mapping is normalized and validated for:
      - `china-mainland`
      - `us-virginia`
      - `singapore`
    - custom Qwen base URLs are allowed only when the region is explicitly `custom`.
    - official region/base-URL mismatches now fail loudly instead of silently using the wrong endpoint.
  - Hardened `/server.ts` AI execution route so provider family is now derived from the canonical model metadata instead of trusting the client-supplied provider hint.
  - Hardened `/server.ts` test-connection route so it can validate env-backed provider runtime resolution and region/endpoint selection, while still allowing explicit override inputs for focused admin diagnostics only.
  - Refactored `/server/aiProviders.ts` provider adapters to accept resolved runtime metadata instead of raw api-key/base-url primitives and added richer diagnostic logging for:
    - `toolId`
    - provider
    - canonical model ID
    - resolved endpoint
    - region
    - env credential resolution state
  - Extended Gemini server execution to normalize inline image output into a `data:` URL so backend-routed Gemini image generation can remain compatible with the existing image tool result surface.
  - Updated `/src/ai/services/aiExecutor.ts` so standard generation flows no longer send `x-api-key` or request-body provider secrets to the backend.
  - Changed execution-mode resolution to backend-authoritative for the normal model-routing path so live secrets and endpoint ownership stay server-side.
  - Kept the dormant frontend Gemini execution path for explicit client-approved use only, but removed its implicit secret fallback so it cannot silently become the default runtime again.
  - Added `/src/ai/fallbackPolicy.ts` with explicit same-provider fallback candidates, but disabled automatic fallback by default to avoid silent cross-provider switching; failures now preserve the originally selected model unless a future policy intentionally enables automatic fallback.
  - Updated `/src/auth/hooks/useModelManagement.ts` so client model config is now metadata-only; selector/display helpers no longer inject provider API keys into frontend runtime objects.
  - Sanitized `/.env.example` so the example file no longer contains live-looking AI or email secrets and now documents the env-backed provider variables clearly.
  - Removed an unused client-side `GoogleGenAI` instantiation from `/src/components/LiveVoice.tsx` so the browser no longer carries an unnecessary direct env-secret assumption in that UI-only placeholder flow.
- Added:
  - Canonical model registry with verified aliases and runtime metadata.
  - Tool-scoped selection resolver module.
  - Explicit fallback-policy module.
  - Server-side provider runtime/env resolver with Qwen region protection.
  - Focused regression tests in `/tests/modelRouting.test.ts`.
  - `npm run test:model-routing` script.
- Removed:
  - Implicit dependence of tool selectors on the global selected model as their fallback seed.
  - Live execution dependence on client-provided API keys and client-provided Qwen base URLs.
  - Trust in client-supplied provider family for backend routing.
  - Real-looking secrets from `/.env.example`.
- Risks / Dependencies:
  - The canonical registry is now the source of truth for selector exposure and provider routing; adding new models in the future must happen through `/src/ai/models/modelRegistry.ts` with real runtime metadata rather than ad-hoc array entries.
  - Qwen compatible-mode execution is intentionally limited to the verified chat/vision path; future Qwen image/video models should not be reintroduced into the live selector surface without a dedicated official endpoint adapter.
  - Global `selectedModelId` still exists in `AuthContext` for backward compatibility with older settings/admin surfaces, but live generation tools now intentionally use only their own tool-scoped selector state.
  - `npm run lint` still reports pre-existing unrelated TypeScript issues in auth, result preview, email delivery, and exporters that were already outside this scope.

    - adds a route-local error fallback so lazy route failures no longer rely on a global full-page crash boundary
  - Refactored `src/App.tsx` route loading:
    - replaced the old bare `renderLazyRoute(...)` helper with the new guarded boundary
    - introduced preloadable route definitions for the primary tool workspaces (`projects`, `images`, `image-editor`, `videos`, `infographic`, `library`, `history`, `chat`, `live`, `tools`)

  - Preserved the known-good quiz generation path:
    - `/generate` remains the eager shared assessment entry surface
    - no behavior was changed in `Dashboard` / quiz generation beyond normalizing the surrounding route architecture
  - Protection against recurrence:
    - no lazy route can remain on the workspace loader forever without timing out into a recoverable state
    - route-level diagnostics now identify which workspace route stalled instead of leaving only an ambiguous spinner
- Verification:
  - `npm run build` passed outside the sandbox on 2026-03-25 after the guarded/preloaded route refactor.
  - Manual dev-runtime probes confirmed the affected route modules were being served by Vite, which reinforced that the shared route-loading lifecycle itself needed hardening rather than one-off page rewrites.
- Notes:
  - This pass intentionally avoided blindly removing code splitting from every page. Primary tool routes are now preloaded lazily instead of being permanently forced into the initial bundle, balancing startup performance with reliable workspace entry.

[2026-03-25]
- Area: Dev Startup / Security Headers / Render Pipeline Recovery
- Files: `/server/securityHeaders.ts`, `/ZOOTOPIA_PROJECT_LEDGER.txt`
- Summary: Fixed the persistent blank white screen on the real `npm run dev` startup path by correcting the development Content Security Policy so Vite's inline React refresh preamble can execute and the client app can actually bootstrap.
- Reason: End-to-end forensic verification of the real dev startup pipeline showed the server was returning HTML routes successfully, but it also applied `script-src 'self'` in development. Vite React dev mode injects an inline module preamble before `/@vite/client`, so the browser was allowed to fetch the assets but could still block the actual startup bootstrap and leave the app on an empty shell.
- Technical Details:
  - Verified the live `npm run dev` path through `server.ts`, not just the static build path.
  - Confirmed `/`, `/login`, and `/generate` were all returning `200` from the real dev server while serving Vite HTML that includes an inline React refresh preamble.
  - Identified the CSP mismatch:
    - HTML included an inline `<script type="module">` refresh preamble from Vite React dev mode
    - `server/securityHeaders.ts` was emitting `script-src 'self'` in development
    - that combination is incompatible and can produce a persistent blank white screen even though the routes and assets are reachable
  - Updated `server/securityHeaders.ts`:
    - introduced a `scriptSources` array
    - keeps production CSP strict
    - adds `'unsafe-inline'` to `script-src` only when `isProduction === false`
    - added an architecture comment explaining that this is a Vite-development requirement, not a production relaxation
  - Post-fix verification:
    - fresh dev-server probe showed the CSP header now includes `script-src 'self' 'unsafe-inline'`
    - `/`, `/login`, and `/generate` continued to respond successfully on the live dev server
    - live Chrome DOM capture on `/login` showed mounted UI output (visible spinner/root content) instead of a blank document body
- Added:
  - Development-only CSP compatibility for Vite React startup
  - Architecture comment documenting why dev CSP must differ from production here
- Removed:
  - The dev-only CSP condition that effectively blocked Vite's inline startup preamble
- Risks / Dependencies:
  - This relaxation is intentionally scoped to development only; production CSP remains strict and unchanged.
  - Future changes to dev security headers must account for how Vite/React inject their startup preamble, or the blank-screen failure can return.
- Notes:
  - This fix targets the real run path used by `npm run dev`, which goes through `server.ts`, security headers, and Vite middleware together.
  - Registration and fast-access modes live inside the shared login surface rather than separate routes, so restoring the login mount path restores access to those auth modes without changing their internal state contracts.

- Summary: Hardened admin/user separation by introducing one canonical frontend access-control helper layer, aligning route and navigation gating with normalized admin identity rules, clearing stale admin-scoped state on downgraded sessions, and correcting a user support route that had drifted into the admin-only route bucket.
- Reason: The backend and Firestore rules were already strong, but the frontend still contained several brittle raw role/adminLevel checks (`'Admin'`, `'primary'`) and one important route-classification mismatch: `/internal-chat` was implemented as a normal user "chat with admin" workspace yet the authenticated shell still treated it like an admin-only route. That combination risked legacy-data privilege drift, stale admin-state leakage, and incorrect route visibility behavior.
- Technical Details:
  - Added `src/auth/accessControl.ts` as the canonical frontend normalization boundary for:
    - role normalization
    - admin-level normalization
    - temporary-scope exclusion
    - reserved-admin identity resolution
    - primary-admin detection
  - Updated `AuthContext` so frontend `isAdmin` now comes from the shared access-control helper instead of duplicating inline normalization logic. This keeps route guards, admin UI, and auth hydration aligned on one rule set.
  - Hardened `ProtectedRoute` so:
    - `primaryAdminOnly` uses canonical primary-admin resolution
    - non-admin verification/status redirects rely on resolved admin identity instead of raw `user.role`
    - transient auth-provider assumptions are guarded more safely
  - Hardened `Sidebar` and `MainLayout` so admin-only navigation, admin-level badges, unlimited-credit treatment, and low-credit banners now follow normalized admin identity instead of brittle raw string checks.
  - Reclassified `/internal-chat` as a normal authenticated support surface instead of an admin-only route:
    - removed it from the admin-only deep-link prefix allowlist in `App.tsx`
    - changed the route wrapper from `<ProtectedRoute adminOnly>` to the standard authenticated `<ProtectedRoute>`
    - removed it from `ADMIN_WORKSPACE_ROUTE_IDS`
    - added it to `SECONDARY_WORKSPACE_ROUTE_IDS`
    - documented in `workspaceRoutes.ts` that the historical `adminChat` key is preserved only for import stability and does not mean the route is admin-only
  - Hardened `useAuthListeners` so non-admin sessions immediately clear admin-scoped caches (`allUsers`, admin-wide `userRequests`) before lower-privilege listeners attach. This prevents stale admin data from surviving role refresh, downgrade, or account switching.
  - Updated `useUserManagement`, `useUsageManagement`, and `useAuthActions` to use the shared access-control helper instead of raw role/adminLevel comparisons. This keeps admin-side capability checks, admin claim synchronization, and unlimited-usage behavior aligned with the same canonical rule set.
  - Tightened admin moderation protection in `useUserManagement` so protected accounts are now blocked consistently across approve/reject/reactivate flows instead of only some moderation paths.
  - Updated mixed user/admin UI surfaces that depended on raw role checks to use canonical admin identity:
    - `ModelSelector`
    - `Settings`
    - `ImageEditorPage`
    - `Account`
    - `InfographicGeneratorPage`
    - `AdminSettings`
    - `AdminPanel`
    - `AdminUserProfile`
    - `CommunicationCenter`
  - Audited but intentionally preserved the authoritative backend and data-security layers because they were already correctly serving as the real security boundary:
    - `server.ts` admin routes remain protected by backend `adminMiddleware`
    - `firestore.rules` already restrict admin collections (`admin_inbox`, `admin_chat_messages`, admin monitoring/billing collections, etc.) to admin callers or owned resources as appropriate
    - this pass aligned the frontend UX/auth interpretation with those existing backend/data boundaries rather than replacing them
- Verification:
  - Ran `npm run build` successfully after the hardening pass. Production build completed with the existing chunk-size warnings only; no new TypeScript or bundling failures were introduced.
  - Ran `npm run test:security` successfully.
