[tests/documentRuntime.test.ts](tests/documentRuntime.test.ts), [tests/documentRuntimeSmoke.ts](tests/documentRuntimeSmoke.ts), [ZOOTOPIA_PROJECT_LEDGER.txt](ZOOTOPIA_PROJECT_LEDGER.txt)
- Summary: Introduced a backend-owned document runtime that centralizes document intake, local extraction, owner-scoped artifact generation, actor-scoped runtime coordination, prompt-context resolution, and dormant direct-file-to-model preparation without removing the current feature modules or breaking the existing upload-first workflow.
- Reason: The previous platform state still relied on frontend extraction plus `DocumentContext.extractedText` as the de facto cross-tool source of truth. That was incompatible with multi-user-safe ownership, strict admin/user runtime isolation, future direct-file dispatch, and production-grade runtime coordination.
- Technical Details:
  - Added `server/documentRuntime/` as the canonical backend layer for document lifecycle concerns:
    - `documentIntakeService.ts` now owns upload registration, local extraction, artifact persistence, and active-document registration.
    - `documentArtifactStore.ts` persists authoritative Firestore metadata for `runtime_documents`, `runtime_document_artifacts`, and future admin-audit access events.
    - `documentStorage.ts` stores source files and extracted artifact payloads in owner-scoped workspace paths under `runtime/document-workspaces/users/{id}/...` and `runtime/document-workspaces/admins/{id}/...`.
    - `runtimeStateService.ts` uses Redis-first keying for active document refs, operation state, cancellation, and locks (`zootopia:runtime:{scope}:{actorId}:...`) with an explicit local in-process fallback for unprovisioned dev/CI environments only.
    - `promptContextResolver.ts` is now the canonical local-extraction resolver that verifies ownership and resolves prompt-ready file context from owner-scoped artifacts instead of trusting raw browser text as the authoritative source.
    - `directModelFileDispatchService.ts` and `providerFileCapabilityRegistry.ts` establish a separate direct-file-to-model preparation path that remains dormant/inactive by default.
  - Added new authenticated document routes in `server.ts`:
    - `POST /api/documents/intake`
    - `GET /api/documents/:documentId/artifact`
    - `GET /api/documents/:documentId/context`
    - `DELETE /api/documents/:documentId/artifact`
    - `POST /api/documents/:documentId/cancel`
    - `POST /api/documents/:documentId/direct-dispatch/prepare`
  - Preserved backend authority and admin/user isolation:
    - document routes use authenticated actor context derived from backend role resolution
    - artifact lookup is owner-scoped by actor ID plus workspace scope (`user` vs `admin`)
    - admin/user runtime namespaces remain separated and cross-actor document access is not opened implicitly
  - Added Redis client dependency (`redis`) and formal runtime config in `server/documentRuntime/config.ts`.
  - Intentionally did not force BullMQ in this phase:
    - current extraction still completes in-request
    - the deployment contract does not yet expose a dedicated worker process
    - `jobOrchestrationService.ts` now centralizes operation-state transitions so BullMQ-backed workers can be attached later without changing route handlers or tool contracts
  - Introduced one shared upload policy module in `src/upload/documentFilePolicy.ts` so browser upload validation and backend intake rules stay aligned on size, extensions, MIME normalization, and image-type detection.
  - Preserved the existing premium upload UX while moving authority to the backend:
    - `AssessmentDashboard.tsx` now validates locally, sends the file to `/api/documents/intake`, mirrors the returned owner-scoped runtime metadata into `DocumentContext`, and cleans up prior document runtime state on replace/remove
    - `DocumentContext` and `documentState` were extended with backend runtime fields (`artifactId`, `sourceFileId`, `ownerRole`, `workspaceScope`, `processingPathway`, `runtimeOperationId`) but remain the frontend compatibility mirror rather than the system of record
  - Extended the AI execution contract so document-aware tools can pass `documentContextRef` (and future `directFileDispatch`) through:
    - `src/ai/types.ts`
    - `src/ai/services/aiRouter.ts`
    - `src/ai/services/aiExecutor.ts`
    - `src/services/geminiService.ts`
    - `src/ai/providers/qwenProvider.ts`
  - Updated the major document-aware tools to send backend document refs while preserving their current UI/business logic:
    - assessment quiz generation
    - analysis workspace
    - chatbot
    - study tools
    - infographic generator
  - Current default active pathway:
    - `local_extraction`
    - extracts text or multimodal image marker payloads into reusable owner-scoped artifacts
    - AI requests resolve prompt context from the backend artifact store when `documentContextRef` is present
  - Dormant pathway foundation:
    - `direct_file_to_model`
    - separate preparation contract only
    - disabled by default unless explicitly enabled later
    - intentionally not blended into the local-extraction prompt resolver contract
  - Current extraction-engine scope:
    - active native extraction for PDF text, DOCX, spreadsheets, plain text
    - image files preserve the existing stable `[IMAGE_DATA:...]` multimodal marker contract for downstream model routing
    - OCR/hybrid schema slots now exist in the artifact contract, but dedicated OCR worker execution is still a future follow-up rather than silently faked in this pass
- Compatibility / Future Rules:
  - Do not reintroduce raw cross-tool dependency on `currentExtractedText` or equivalent anonymous globals as the authoritative source of truth.
  - New document-aware tools should consume document context through backend-owned `documentContextRef` resolution and keep any UI mirror state inside `DocumentContext` compatibility boundaries only.
  - Keep admin-only document operations explicit, permission-checked, and auditable. Do not blur admin runtime storage with normal user runtime state.
  - If direct file-to-model mode is enabled later, implement provider execution through the separate dispatch layer rather than overloading the local-extraction resolver contract.
  - If OCR/heavy extraction becomes long-running, attach BullMQ/workers through `jobOrchestrationService.ts` and `runtimeStateService.ts` instead of bypassing the new runtime layer.
- Verification:
  - Installed the Redis client dependency and confirmed the frontend production build still succeeds with `npm run build` (existing chunk-size warnings only).
  - Ran `tests/documentRuntimeSmoke.ts` successfully; the smoke script verified actor-scoped runtime keys, dormant direct-file strategy resolution, native text extraction, and image marker artifact preservation.
  - Ran `npm run lint`; the remaining TypeScript failures are currently pre-existing unrelated issues in other areas (`server/adminAccountDirectoryService.ts`, `src/admin/components/CommunicationCenter.tsx`, `src/App.tsx`, `src/auth/hooks/useAuthActions.ts`, `src/services/emailDeliveryService.ts`, `src/utils/exporters.ts`, existing admin-account test typing). The document-runtime-specific type issues introduced in this pass were resolved before recording this entry.

- Date: 2026-03-26
- Area: Layered Document Extraction Hardening / Prompt-Ready Artifact Quality / Actor-Scoped Cleanup Safety
- Summary: Strengthened the existing document-runtime backbone into a clearer 2026-style layered extraction pipeline without rebuilding the project: file typing is now signature-aware, normalized output is more structurally organized for AI consumption, prompt-context packaging is centralized, stale/cancelled document writes are blocked before they can resurrect old artifacts, and replacement/invalidation flows now preserve actor-scoped safety more explicitly.
- Reason:
  - The repository already had the right backbone for owner-scoped document runtime and shared prompt resolution, so the safe move was to harden quality and lifecycle guarantees instead of creating a second extraction system.
  - The biggest risks were structural flattening, duplicated prompt payloads, weak stale-write protection during cancel/replace, and future contributors bypassing the canonical prompt-context resolver.
- Layers Preserved And Strengthened:
  - Layer 1 `Upload Intake Layer`
    - `server/documentRuntime/documentIntakeService.ts` now validates uploads before persisting source files, keeps the existing authenticated intake route contract intact, and checks cancellation/stale state between extraction phases.
    - `src/features/assessment-tool/pages/AssessmentDashboard.tsx` now explicitly invalidates the previous backend document runtime before promoting a replacement upload, while preserving the current React 19 upload UX and dashboard flow.
  - Layer 2 `File Typing And Strategy Resolution Layer`
    - `server/documentRuntime/fileTypeDetectionService.ts` now combines extension-based inference with binary-signature detection for safer PDF/image identification and records richer hints into extraction metadata.
    - Current supported production inputs remain conservative: PDF, DOCX, XLSX/XLS/CSV, TXT, and images. PPTX detection remains non-authoritative until slide-aware extraction is fully verified in the real stack.
  - Layer 3 `Native Extraction Layer`
    - `server/documentRuntime/python/extract_document.py` continues to use the pinned libraries:
      - `pypdf==6.9.2`
      - `python-docx==1.2.0`
      - `openpyxl==3.1.5`
    - Native extraction now preserves more structure:
      - PDF pages remain page-scoped.
      - DOCX paragraph styles are translated into title/heading/subheading/list/table-aware blocks when possible.
      - spreadsheets remain sheet-aware and table-oriented rather than being flattened to one blob.
  - Layer 4 `OCR And Document Vision Layer`
    - The Python worker continues to pin `paddleocr==3.4.0`.
    - OCR normalization now preserves block order, per-block confidence, and bounding boxes more clearly.
    - OCR is still layered conservatively: images are supported from phase one, PDF OCR is attempted through the same OCR layer when PaddleOCR runtime is available, and the existing multimodal image marker fallback remains intact when OCR infrastructure is unavailable.
  - Layer 5 `Advanced Document Understanding Layer`
    - The Python worker continues to pin `docling==2.82.0`.
    - `server/documentRuntime/documentStructureNormalizer.ts` now uses Docling as enrichment metadata instead of blindly appending a duplicate full-document appendix into the prompt context.
    - `server/documentRuntime/extractionShared.ts` now derives a stronger heading tree, grouped sections, cleaner markdown reconstruction, table/list rendering, and source metadata for prompt orchestration.
  - Layer 6 `Extraction Coordinator Layer`
    - `server/documentRuntime/extractionCoordinator.ts` remains the canonical orchestration layer that chooses native/OCR/hybrid execution and emits one canonical artifact envelope.
    - `server/documentRuntime/documentArtifactStore.ts` now promotes artifacts to ready state only through a guarded Firestore transaction path; cancelled/deleted documents cannot be resurrected by late extraction writes.
    - `server/documentRuntime/jobOrchestrationService.ts` retains the BullMQ-ready boundary but still avoids introducing a worker queue prematurely. BullMQ remains intentionally deferred until extraction becomes truly long-running outside the request lifecycle.
  - Layer 7 `Canonical Extracted Artifact Layer`
    - Canonical artifact fields remain centered on:
      - `artifactId`
      - `documentId`
      - `workflowId` as the active workflow/session-scoped identifier
      - `sourceFileId`
      - `actorId` / `actorRole`
      - `fileType`
      - `extractionStrategy`
      - `status`
      - `originalFilePath`
      - `finalExtractedTextPath`
      - `structuredJsonPath`
      - `normalizedMarkdownPath`
      - `pageMapPath`
      - `ocrBlocksPath`
      - timestamps and expiration fields
    - Output formats remain:
      - structured JSON
      - normalized markdown
      - clean extracted text
    - The normalized markdown is now closer to a document reconstruction:
      - source metadata section
      - structural overview
      - explicit page boundaries
      - heading/subheading hierarchy
      - bullet preservation
      - markdown table rendering
      - OCR/extraction notes separated from the main body
  - Layer 8 `Temporary Actor-Scoped Storage Layer`
    - `server/documentRuntime/actorWorkspaceResolver.ts` continues to enforce server-controlled owner-scoped paths:
      - `runtime/document-workspaces/users/{userId}/workflows/{workflowId}/documents/{documentId}/...`
      - `runtime/document-workspaces/admins/{adminId}/workflows/{workflowId}/documents/{documentId}/...`
    - This satisfies the actor/session/workflow isolation requirement without introducing global shared extraction files.
  - Layer 9 `Shared Prompt Context Layer`
    - `server/documentRuntime/promptContextResolver.ts` remains the single shared resolver for tools that consume extracted document context.
    - `server/documentRuntime/promptContextAssembler.ts` is now the centralized packaging layer for prompt-ready document context:
      - file-context body
      - document summary
      - structural insights
      - condensed structured document data
      - human-readable page-map summary
      - heading-tree summary
      - OCR summary when present
      - artifact-path metadata
    - Critical preserve rule:
      - Tools must continue to pass `documentContextRef` and let the backend resolve context.
      - New tools must not independently re-read extracted files or rebuild document prompts ad hoc.
  - Layer 10 `Prompt Orchestration Integration Layer`
    - Existing orchestration contracts were preserved:
      - `src/ai/services/aiExecutor.ts`
      - `src/ai/services/aiRouter.ts`
      - `src/ai/services/promptOrchestrator.ts`
      - `/api/ai/execute` in `server.ts`
    - The active document-aware flow remains:
      - frontend sends `documentContextRef`
      - backend resolves owner-scoped artifact through `promptContextResolver`
      - orchestration receives the same normalized markdown plus structured side-channel context for every tool
    - This keeps quiz generation, analysis, chatbot, study tools, and infographic flows on the same backend-owned extracted context instead of per-tool file parsing.
  - Layer 11 `Result Rendering Layer`
    - Existing renderers and preview/export systems were intentionally preserved.
    - This pass only changes how document context is prepared upstream; it does not redesign tool result surfaces.
  - Layer 12 `Final AI Result Retention Layer`
    - `src/services/resultService.ts` still enforces the 3-day final-result rule and now exposes the TTL field name (`expiresAt`) and policy version more explicitly.
    - `firebase-blueprint.json` now reflects the Firestore result contract more accurately:
      - `title`
      - `type`
      - `sourceTool`
      - `createdAt`
      - `expiresAt`
      - `planAtCreation`
      - `retentionDaysAtCreation`
      - `retentionPolicyVersion`
      - `status`
    - Important preserve rule:
      - Temporary extracted artifacts stay on actor-scoped server storage and are indexed only by runtime metadata.
      - Final AI result records remain the only long-lived extraction-adjacent content intentionally retained in Firestore.
      - Firestore TTL must be configured on the `results.expiresAt` field in infrastructure/admin settings; repository code only writes the canonical TTL field and policy metadata.
- Runtime Redis / Coordination Design:
  - `server/documentRuntime/runtimeStateService.ts` remains the actor-scoped runtime registry for:
    - active document refs
    - per-document extraction state
    - operation status
    - cancellation flags
    - extraction locks
  - Existing Redis key design remains aligned with the intended namespace:
    - `zootopia:runtime:user:{userId}:active-doc`
    - `zootopia:runtime:user:{userId}:extract:{documentId}`
    - `zootopia:runtime:user:{userId}:ops:{operationId}`
    - matching admin-scoped variants
  - Redis remains runtime coordination only, not the durable store for extracted content.
- Cleanup / Invalidation Lifecycle:
  - `server/documentRuntime/documentArtifactStore.ts` now blocks late artifact promotion when a document is already cancelled/deleted.
  - `server/documentRuntime/cleanupCoordinator.ts` now requests cancellation before invalidation so in-flight extraction is less likely to race with cleanup.
  - `DocumentArtifactStore` now records artifact invalidation metadata (`invalidatedAt`, `invalidationReason`) for safer runtime auditing.
  - Expired document-artifact access is now handled more safely:
    - expired artifacts are invalidated on access
    - workspace files are removed
    - tools receive a no-longer-ready response instead of stale content
  - Frontend replacement flow now invalidates the prior backend document runtime before the next upload is promoted.
- Sensitive Areas Future Contributors Must Preserve:
  - Do not bypass `promptContextResolver` for document-aware tools.
  - Do not store full extracted artifacts in Firestore as the canonical extraction store.
  - Do not collapse actor scope:
    - user and admin temp paths must stay isolated
    - runtime keys must stay actor-scoped
    - explicit admin governance access must remain auditable
  - Do not append duplicated raw structural payloads into the final prompt just because Docling returns markdown; structural enrichment must stay selective and prompt-efficient.
  - Do not remove the guarded stale-write path in `documentArtifactStore.ts`; it is what prevents cancel/delete/replace races from reviving old artifacts.
  - Do not reintroduce frontend-owned extraction authority. The browser may mirror state, but backend runtime remains authoritative.
- Files Introduced Or Materially Changed In This Hardening Pass:
  - `server/documentRuntime/fileTypeDetectionService.ts`
  - `server/documentRuntime/extractionShared.ts`
  - `server/documentRuntime/documentStructureNormalizer.ts`
  - `server/documentRuntime/promptContextAssembler.ts`
  - `server/documentRuntime/promptContextResolver.ts`
  - `server/documentRuntime/documentArtifactStore.ts`
  - `server/documentRuntime/documentIntakeService.ts`
  - `server/documentRuntime/cleanupCoordinator.ts`
  - `server/documentRuntime/python/extract_document.py`
  - `src/features/assessment-tool/pages/AssessmentDashboard.tsx`
  - `src/services/resultService.ts`
  - `firebase-blueprint.json`
  - tests:
    - `tests/documentRuntime.test.ts`
    - `tests/documentPromptContextResolver.test.ts`
    - `tests/documentStructureNormalizer.test.ts`
    - `tests/fileTypeDetectionService.test.ts`
    - `tests/documentArtifactStore.test.ts`
- Verification:
  - `python -m py_compile server/documentRuntime/python/extract_document.py` passed.
  - `node_modules\.bin\tsx.cmd tests\documentRuntimeSmoke.ts` passed.
  - Focused document-runtime suite passed outside the sandbox after sandbox process-spawn restrictions blocked the local Node test runner:
    - `tests/documentRuntime.test.ts`
    - `tests/documentPromptContextResolver.test.ts`
    - `tests/documentStructureNormalizer.test.ts`
    - `tests/fileTypeDetectionService.test.ts`
    - `tests/documentArtifactStore.test.ts`
  - `npm run lint` still fails only in unrelated pre-existing areas outside this extraction hardening pass:
    - `server/adminAccountDirectoryService.ts`
    - `src/admin/components/CommunicationCenter.tsx`
    - `src/App.tsx`

- Date: 2026-03-27
- Area: Deployment Configuration / Explicit Python Extraction Dependency Discovery
- Summary: Added explicit Render and Netlify deployment contracts so the nested Python extraction requirements file at `server/documentRuntime/python/requirements.txt` is no longer left to hosting-platform auto-detection, while preserving the existing single-service Node + embedded Python-worker architecture.
- Reason:
  - The repository already runs as one backend service via `server.ts`, with production serving the built SPA from `dist` and document extraction spawning `server/documentRuntime/python/extract_document.py` directly.
  - Before this pass, no root deployment config referenced the nested Python requirements file, there was no production `start` script, and the backend still bound to a hardcoded `3000`, which is unsafe on platforms that inject `PORT`.
- Deployment Config Added / Updated:
  - Added `render.yaml`
    - Uses the current single-service architecture instead of inventing a separate Python service.
    - Build command is now explicit: `npm run deploy:render:build`
    - Start command is now explicit: `NODE_ENV=production DOCUMENT_RUNTIME_PYTHON_EXECUTABLE=python npm run start`
    - This keeps the backend entrypoint aligned with the real app contract in `server.ts` and keeps the nested Python worker path visible in deployment configuration.
    - The Render build path intentionally keeps the `tsx` runtime available because `tsconfig.json` is `noEmit` and there is no compiled `server.js` artifact yet.
  - Added `netlify.toml`
    - Declares Netlify as frontend-only hosting for the current repository architecture.
    - Build command is now explicit: `npm run deploy:netlify:build`
    - Publish directory is explicit: `dist`
    - Added an SPA redirect so static route refreshes continue to resolve to `index.html` instead of relying on platform guessing.
  - Updated `package.json`
    - Added `start` so production hosting no longer has to infer how to launch the backend.
    - Added `verify:python-runtime`
    - Added `deploy:render:build`
    - Added `deploy:netlify:build`
  - Added `tools/deploymentRuntime.mjs`
    - Central deployment helper that:
      - verifies `server/documentRuntime/python/requirements.txt`
      - verifies `server/documentRuntime/python/extract_document.py`
      - prints the exact requirements path and pinned extraction packages during build
      - fails fast if the nested requirements file is missing
    - Render build mode now also runs:
      - `python --version`
      - `npm ci`
      - `python -m pip install --upgrade pip`
      - `python -m pip install -r server/documentRuntime/python/requirements.txt`
      - `npm run build`
    - Netlify build mode intentionally does not install or execute the Python runtime; it verifies visibility of the nested requirements path, logs that Netlify is frontend-only, and then runs the Vite frontend build.
  - Updated `server.ts`
    - Replaced the hardcoded port with `process.env.PORT` plus a safe `3000` fallback so Render-style managed hosts can bind correctly without breaking local development.
  - Updated `.env.example`
    - Added explicit deployment/runtime environment visibility for:
      - `PORT`
      - `REDIS_URL`
      - `DOCUMENT_RUNTIME_PYTHON_EXECUTABLE`
      - `DOCUMENT_RUNTIME_PYTHON_EXTRACTION_ENABLED`
      - `DOCUMENT_RUNTIME_PYTHON_SCRIPT_PATH`
- Python Version Visibility:
  - No root `.python-version` or `runtime.txt` was added in this pass.
  - Reason: the repository did not already encode an authoritative cross-platform Python version contract for the current extraction stack, so inventing one here would have been a behavioral decision rather than a documentation-only improvement.
  - Instead, deployment now makes Python runtime visibility explicit by:
    - requiring `python --version` during the Render build path
    - failing clearly if the nested Python extraction requirements file or worker script is missing
    - documenting the current deployment expectation instead of hiding it behind platform detection
- What Is No Longer Implicit:
  - Render no longer has to guess where the Python extraction dependencies live.
  - Netlify no longer appears to be a backend-capable Python runtime for this repository.
  - Production startup no longer depends on undocumented knowledge that `server.ts` is the backend entrypoint.
  - Managed hosting no longer depends on a hardcoded port assumption.
- Sensitive Areas Future Contributors Must Preserve:
  - Keep `server/documentRuntime/python/requirements.txt` as the authoritative extraction dependency file unless the deployment helper and hosting configs are updated in the same change.
  - Do not move `server/documentRuntime/python/extract_document.py` without updating `tools/deploymentRuntime.mjs` and the related runtime configuration.
  - Do not configure Netlify as if it runs the backend Python extractor unless the architecture is intentionally split and documented.
  - Keep Render aligned to the existing `server.ts` single-service contract unless a deliberate multi-service refactor is performed.
  - Preserve `PORT` host binding and avoid reintroducing a hardcoded production port.
- Files Introduced Or Materially Changed In This Deployment Pass:
  - `render.yaml`
  - `netlify.toml`
  - `tools/deploymentRuntime.mjs`
  - `package.json`
  - `server.ts`
  - `.env.example`
- Verification:
  - `node tools/deploymentRuntime.mjs verify`
  - additional build verification should continue to use the platform-specific scripts:
    - `npm run deploy:render:build`
    - `npm run deploy:netlify:build`

- Area: Deployment Configuration / Runtime Version Contract / Raw-Host Visibility
- Summary: Tightened the deployment layer by adding explicit repo-root runtime version files, wiring those versions into the canonical deployment manifest, and teaching the shared deployment helper to fail fast when the runtime contract drifts from the manifest.
- Reason:
  - The repository already had the shared manifest/helper plus Docker-backed backend platform adapters, but Node/Python version intent still lived mostly in inference and documentation instead of the same deployment contract that governs the Python extraction requirements path.
  - That made the Python dependency path explicit while leaving local/VPS runtime selection less discoverable than it should be.

      - `.nvmrc`
      - `.node-version`
      - `.python-version`
  - Added `preferredBootstrapCommands` under the Python manifest contract so local/server bootstrap prefers Python 3.11 before falling back to another interpreter on PATH.
- Helper Refinement:
  - Updated `tools/deploymentRuntime.mjs`
    - verifies the repo-root version files and fails fast if they disagree with the shared manifest
    - logs the preferred backend runtime contract during deployment verification
    - resolves bootstrap Python candidates through the manifest instead of assuming plain `python` / `python3` is always the right interpreter
  - This keeps the runtime-version contract discoverable and enforceable in the same deployment layer that already protects `server/documentRuntime/python/requirements.txt`.
- Additional Config Alignment:

  - Updated `Makefile`

  - Updated `Dockerfile`

  - Updated docs:
    - `README.md`
    - `DEPLOYMENT.md`
- Sensitive Areas Future Contributors Must Preserve:
  - Keep the repo-root version files aligned with `deployment/runtime-manifest.json` whenever the backend runtime contract changes.
  - Keep Docker, raw-host bootstrap, and the shared helper aligned in the same change when updating Node or Python versions.
  - Do not change the Python extraction dependency path without updating the helper and manifest together.

- Date: 2026-03-27
- Area: Deployment Configuration / Docker-First Backend Contract Hardening
- Summary: Hardened the multi-platform deployment layer so the canonical Python extraction dependency path remains explicit across local, Linux/VPS, Render, Netlify, Vercel, Railway, Fly.io, Google Cloud Run, and Docker, while removing the remaining Render-native runtime guesswork and fixing Windows helper execution for repo-local Python paths.
- Reason:
  - The repository already had a manifest/helper deployment layer, but two practical gaps remained:
    - `tools/deploymentRuntime.mjs` invoked repo-local Windows executables through PowerShell incorrectly when paths contained spaces, which broke deep Python runtime verification for `.venv`.
    - Render still depended on a native Node service path, which left Python runtime behavior partially dependent on host image assumptions rather than the same explicit contract used by the other backend-capable platforms.
  - The requested deployment system needs one canonical dependency definition plus explicit, honest platform adapters.
- Deployment Strategy Now In Force:
  - Hybrid strategy:
    - shared manifest plus shared helper for validation/bootstrap
    - shared Docker backend for backend-capable managed hosts
    - explicit frontend-only contracts for static hosts
  - Backend-capable managed hosts now converge on the shared `Dockerfile`:
    - Render
    - Railway
    - Fly.io
    - Google Cloud Run
    - generic Docker/container hosts
  - Local development and generic Linux/VPS keep the raw-host helper path:
    - `npm run setup:local`
    - `./tools/setup-linux-server.sh`
    - `./tools/start-linux-server.sh`
  - Netlify and Vercel remain explicitly frontend-only.
- Canonical Deployment Source Of Truth:
  - `deployment/runtime-manifest.json`
    - Still references the canonical Python dependency file:
      - `server/documentRuntime/python/requirements.txt`
    - Still references the canonical Python worker:
      - `server/documentRuntime/python/extract_document.py`
    - Now also records explicit platform contract files for:
      - local development
      - generic Linux server
      - Render
      - Netlify
      - Vercel
      - Railway
      - Fly.io
      - Google Cloud Run
      - Docker
    - `tools/deploymentRuntime.mjs verify` now fails fast if those declared platform contract files are missing.
- Files Updated:
  - `deployment/runtime-manifest.json`
    - Added backend container metadata:
      - `Dockerfile`
      - `/app/.venv/bin/python`
    - Replaced the older coarse `platformIntent` list with explicit `deploymentTargets` metadata and contract file paths.
  - `tools/deploymentRuntime.mjs`
    - Replaced the Windows PowerShell wrapper with direct executable spawning so repo-local paths like `.venv\Scripts\python.exe` work correctly when the workspace path contains spaces.
    - Added deployment-target verification driven from `deployment/runtime-manifest.json`.
    - Improved Python detector failure diagnostics to include stderr/stdout/error/status details instead of a vague empty failure.
  - `package.json`
    - Added `verify:deployment-contract`.
    - Repointed `verify:python-runtime` to the real Python detector so the script name now matches actual behavior.
  - `render.yaml`
    - Switched Render to the shared Docker backend contract instead of a native Node build/start path.
    - Kept `/api/health` explicit.
    - Kept `DOCUMENT_RUNTIME_PYTHON_EXECUTABLE=/app/.venv/bin/python` explicit.
  - `tools/start-linux-server.sh`
    - Added an explicit `node_modules` presence check so raw-host startup fails with a clear instruction instead of a later runtime error.
  - `README.md`
    - Updated the top-level deployment summary to describe the manifest/helper/container split clearly.
  - `DEPLOYMENT.md`
    - Rewrote the deployment guide to document the Docker-first backend contract, the platform matrix, and the difference between deployment-contract verification and deep Python runtime verification.
- Platform Behavior After This Pass:
  - Local development:
    - `npm run setup:local` remains the canonical bootstrap path.
    - `.venv` remains the repo-local Python installation target.
    - deep verification now works correctly against `.venv\Scripts\python.exe` on Windows path-with-spaces workspaces.
  - Generic Linux/VPS:
    - `./tools/setup-linux-server.sh` installs Node dependencies, creates `.venv`, installs the canonical requirements, verifies the Python extractor, and builds the frontend.
    - `./tools/start-linux-server.sh` now fails clearly if either `.venv` or `node_modules` is missing.
  - Render:
    - now uses the shared Docker backend via `render.yaml` + `Dockerfile`.
    - Python dependency installation comes from the container build:
      - `pip install -r server/documentRuntime/python/requirements.txt`
  - Netlify:
    - remains frontend-only via `netlify.toml`.
    - still verifies the canonical deployment contract during build visibility, but does not claim to host the Python extractor.
  - Vercel:
    - remains frontend-only via `vercel.json`.
    - still verifies the canonical deployment contract during build visibility, but does not claim to host the Python extractor.
  - Railway:
    - continues to use `railway.toml` + `Dockerfile`.
  - Fly.io:
    - continues to use `fly.toml` + `Dockerfile`.
  - Google Cloud Run:
    - continues to use `cloudbuild.yaml` + `Dockerfile`.
  - Docker:
    - remains the portability anchor for the backend runtime.
- Runtime Version Visibility:
  - The strongest explicit runtime version contract is still the shared container:
    - `node:22-bookworm-slim`
  - No raw-host `.python-version` or `.node-version` file was added because the repository still does not prove one safe minor-version pin across every local/VPS environment.
  - The helper therefore validates capability directly instead of inventing a version contract.
- Honest Limitations:
  - The backend still runs via `tsx server.ts`, so backend-capable installs still retain devDependencies intentionally.
  - Netlify and Vercel still do not host the Express backend or Python extraction runtime.
  - `verify:python-runtime` is now honest and strict: it will fail until the required Python extraction packages are actually installed into the selected runtime.
- Verification:
  - `node tools/deploymentRuntime.mjs verify`
    - passed after this change.
  - `node tools/deploymentRuntime.mjs python-detect`
    - now reaches the real repo-local Python executable correctly on Windows and fails for the real reason when packages are missing, instead of failing behind the old PowerShell invocation bug.

- Date: 2026-03-27
- Area: Admin Authentication / Infinite Loading / Bounded Claims Sync
- Summary: Fixed the admin-login hang by removing an unbounded admin-claims sync request from the critical profile-hydration path and adding an explicit timeout/fail-safe around the admin login submit flow.
- Root Cause:
  - The admin login path in `src/auth/Login.tsx` awaited `adminLogin(...)`, which awaited `syncUserWithFirestore(...)` in `src/auth/hooks/useAuthActions.ts`.
  - Inside `syncUserWithFirestore(...)`, reserved admin identities triggered `fetch('/api/admin/set-claims', ...)` and awaited it before profile hydration could finish.
  - That request had no timeout and no non-blocking fallback. If the backend route stalled, the browser kept waiting, so the login page stayed on `Authenticating admin...` without success, redirect, error, or recovery.
  - This affected the admin lane specifically because only the reserved-admin branch triggered the custom-claims repair call.
- Files Updated:
  - `src/auth/hooks/useAuthActions.ts`
  - `src/auth/Login.tsx`
  - `ZOOTOPIA_PROJECT_LEDGER.txt`
- Safe Fix Implemented:
  - `src/auth/hooks/useAuthActions.ts`
    - Added `fetchJsonWithTimeout(...)` using `AbortController` for bounded fetch behavior.
    - Added explicit timeout budgets for username lookup and admin-claims sync.
    - Switched reserved-admin claims repair to a bounded background task instead of awaiting it on the critical login/profile-hydration path.
    - Kept structured diagnostics through the existing logger when claims sync fails or times out.
  - `src/auth/Login.tsx`
    - Wrapped `adminLogin(...)` in a hard timeout via `withTimeout(...)`.
    - Added explicit `try/catch/finally` coverage plus structured diagnostics.
    - Ensured the UI leaves `processing` on every failure branch by routing failures through `setError(...)`.
- Why The Spinner Never Ended:
  - The login screen set the status to `Authenticating admin...`, then waited on a promise chain that included a network request with no timeout.
  - Because that promise could remain pending forever, the submit handler never reached success or catch, so the loading state never exited.
  - The broader auth bootstrap logic already had recovery timers, but the admin submit handler itself still had an unbounded promise on its path.
- What Must Be Preserved:
  - Admin claims synchronization must remain non-blocking relative to admin login/profile hydration.
  - Any admin-only verification fetch added in the future must have a bounded timeout and user-visible failure path.
  - Frontend admin detection may assist routing/UX, but backend authorization remains the security boundary.
  - Do not reintroduce awaited network side effects into the critical admin login completion path unless they are explicitly time-bounded and have a safe recovery path.
- Verification:
  - The updated code now guarantees:
    - a timeout on admin username resolution
    - a timeout on reserved-admin claims repair
    - a timeout on the admin login submit path itself
    - a `catch`/error exit instead of indefinite `processing`

- Date: 2026-03-27
- Area: Cross-Platform Dependencies / Native Render Deployment / Linux Install Safety
- Summary: Removed root-pinned Windows-native build binaries from the Node dependency graph, normalized the Vite/Tailwind build-tool ownership, regenerated the lockfile, and switched Render back to a native Node deployment contract instead of Docker.
- Root Cause:
  - `package.json` directly declared Windows-only native packages:
    - `@tailwindcss/oxide-win32-x64-msvc`
    - `lightningcss-win32-x64-msvc`
  - Those packages are host-specific binaries, not cross-platform application dependencies.
  - Because they were pinned at the root project level, Linux hosts such as Render attempted to install them as normal dependencies and failed before Vite/Tailwind could finish setting up.
  - `vite` was also duplicated across `dependencies` and `devDependencies`, which made the build-tool ownership noisier than necessary.
  - `render.yaml` had been switched to a Docker-backed service contract, which no longer matched the requested native Render deployment path.
- Files Updated:
  - `package.json`
  - `package-lock.json`
  - `render.yaml`
  - `deployment/runtime-manifest.json`
  - `README.md`
  - `DEPLOYMENT.md`
  - `ZOOTOPIA_PROJECT_LEDGER.txt`
- Safe Fix Implemented:
  - `package.json`
    - removed direct root dependencies:
      - `@tailwindcss/oxide-win32-x64-msvc`
      - `lightningcss-win32-x64-msvc`
    - moved build-time tooling to `devDependencies`:
      - `@tailwindcss/vite`
      - `@vitejs/plugin-react`
      - `lightningcss`
      - `vite`
    - kept the generic cross-platform packages only.
  - `package-lock.json`
    - regenerated from the corrected manifest so the root package block no longer pins the Windows-only packages directly.
    - remaining platform-native packages are now upstream optional/transitive entries rather than app-level requirements.
  - `render.yaml`
    - switched Render back to native `env: node`
    - explicit build command:
      - `npm run deploy:render:build`
    - explicit start command:
      - `npm run start`
    - explicit environment:
      - `NODE_ENV=production`
      - `DOCUMENT_RUNTIME_PYTHON_EXECUTABLE=.venv/bin/python`
    - kept `/api/health` explicit.
  - `deployment/runtime-manifest.json`
    - reclassified Render from `shared-docker-backend` to `shared-helper-bootstrap`
    - aligned Render contract paths and commands with the native helper-based deployment path
  - `README.md` and `DEPLOYMENT.md`
    - documented Render as native, not Docker-based
    - added a warning against committing OS-specific binary packages to root dependencies
- What Future Contributors Must Preserve:
  - Do not add host-specific binary packages like `*-win32-*`, `*-linux-*`, or similar directly to root `dependencies`.
  - Keep only the generic tool packages in the project manifest and let their optional dependency graph resolve the correct host binary.
  - Keep Render aligned to the native helper-based deployment path unless there is a deliberate, documented platform strategy change.
  - Keep `server/documentRuntime/python/requirements.txt` and `.venv` installation explicit in the Render build helper path.
- Verification:
  - `npm install --package-lock-only --ignore-scripts`
    - completed successfully after rerouting npm cache into a repo-local writable cache directory because the default global cache path was blocked in this environment.
  - `npm run verify:deployment-contract`
    - passed with Render now reported as `shared-helper-bootstrap`.
  - `npm run build`
    - could not be conclusively verified in this environment because the build command either hit sandbox `EPERM` process-spawn limits or stalled without returning a completed result under the available execution environment.
    - This means the dependency-contract fix is implemented and the root Linux blocker is removed, but final end-to-end build confirmation should still be re-run in a normal local shell or the target Render environment.

[2026-03-27]
- Area: Auth / Redis / Session Architecture / Admin + Fast Access Isolation
- Files:
  - `server.ts`

  - `src/auth/session/storage.ts`
  - `src/auth/session/baseAuthSessionManager.ts`
  - `src/auth/session/normalAuthSessionManager.ts`
  - `src/auth/session/fastAccessAuthSessionManager.ts`
  - `src/auth/session/adminAuthSessionManager.ts`
  - `src/auth/session/sessionApi.ts`
  - `src/auth/session/index.ts`
  - `src/components/ProtectedRoute.tsx`
  - `src/components/AuthScopedDocumentBoundary.tsx`

  - `tests/documentRuntimeSmoke.ts`
  - `tests/documentPromptContextResolver.test.ts`
  - `tests/documentCleanupCoordinator.test.ts`
  - `tests/modelRouting.test.ts`
  - `ZOOTOPIA_PROJECT_LEDGER.txt`
- Summary:
  - Refactored the live auth/session/cache path toward three isolated login lanes:
    - `normal`
    - `fast_access`
    - `admin`
  - Added dedicated frontend session managers per auth mode, a richer backend auth-session snapshot model backed by Redis, auth-mode-aware route enforcement for admin pages, auth-mode-aware document runtime scoping, and scoped browser-state cleanup to prevent cross-mode/session leakage.
- Root Cause:
  - The platform previously mixed three different concerns:
    - Firebase identity state
    - loosely persisted browser auth hints
    - role-based UI decisions
  - Admin UI access was still largely keyed off generic admin identity (`isAdmin`) rather than the dedicated admin session lane.
  - Fast Access used an isolated OTP step, but the final platform session still converged on the primary Firebase auth instance, so isolation depended on claims/account metadata and not on separate lifecycle managers.
  - Runtime/document/tool state could survive account or auth-mode switches because several browser and Redis surfaces were not explicitly auth-mode scoped.
  - Older local-storage keys (`zootopia_admin_session`, `zootopia_session_expiry`) and legacy unscoped tool-model keys existed without a single authoritative migration boundary.
- Technical Details:
  - Backend session authority:
    - Added/activated `server/authSessionService.ts` as the live auth-session owner for the current server path.
    - Added richer server-side session metadata:
      - `authType`
      - `sessionState`
      - `sessionSource`
      - `sessionFingerprint`
      - `issuedAt`
      - `refreshedAt`
      - `expiresAt`
      - `lastActivityAt`
      - `rehydrationStatus`
      - `reEntryStatus`
      - `restoreFailureReason`
      - `logoutReason`
      - `adminVerificationStatus`
      - `fastAccessVerificationStatus`
      - `accountCompletenessStatus`
      - cache/session/document-runtime namespace references
    - Added focused session endpoints:
      - `POST /api/auth/session/bootstrap`
      - `POST /api/auth/session/refresh`
      - `POST /api/auth/session/logout`
    - Added expected auth-mode handling to middleware validation so backend routes can distinguish:
      - generic authenticated requests
      - admin-only requests
      - fast-access-only requests
  - Redis/cache organization:
    - Added `server/cache/redisBackedStore.ts` for Redis connection management plus a bounded in-memory fallback for local/dev-safe operation.
    - Active auth-session namespace contract:
      - current snapshot:
        - `zootopia:auth:<authType>:users:<uid>:current`
      - historical/session snapshot:
        - `zootopia:auth:<authType>:users:<uid>:sessions:<sessionId>`
      - invalidation marker:
        - `zootopia:auth:<authType>:users:<uid>:invalidation`
      - derived cache namespace stored in session metadata:
        - `zootopia:auth:<authType>:users:<uid>:cache`
      - derived document-runtime namespace stored in session metadata:
        - `document-runtime:<authType>:<uid>`
    - Document runtime Redis keys were upgraded from role-only/user-only scoping to auth-mode-aware scoping:
      - `zootopia:runtime:<workspaceScope>:<authType>:<actorId>:*`
    - This prevents runtime extraction/active-document collisions between:
      - normal user sessions
      - fast-access sessions
      - admin sessions
  - Session managers and browser persistence:
    - Added dedicated frontend managers:
      - `normalAuthSessionManager`
      - `fastAccessAuthSessionManager`
      - `adminAuthSessionManager`
    - Added browser persistence contract:
      - active mode key:
        - `zootopia_auth_session_mode_v2`
      - per-mode snapshots:
        - `zootopia_auth_session_v2:normal`
        - `zootopia_auth_session_v2:fast_access`
        - `zootopia_auth_session_v2:admin`
    - `AuthContext` now restores from the stored per-mode snapshot in `restoring` state first, then revalidates against Firebase + backend session state before treating the session as ready.
    - Standard email/password and Google login flows now explicitly prime the `normal` auth mode before sign-in.
    - Admin login now explicitly primes the `admin` auth mode before sign-in.
    - Fast Access custom-token sign-in now explicitly primes the `fast_access` auth mode before the primary Firebase session is established.
  - Isolation and invalidation:
    - Logging into one auth mode now clears sibling frontend auth-session managers.
    - Backend bootstrap now invalidates sibling auth-mode Redis sessions for the same uid to avoid stale cross-mode revival.
    - Logout remains scoped to the active auth mode, but replace-on-login now clears old sibling auth-mode remnants more aggressively.
    - `ProtectedRoute` now requires `authMode === 'admin'` for admin-only and primary-admin-only route access instead of trusting generic admin identity alone.
  - Tool/document/browser cache separation:
    - Tool model persistence moved to auth-session-scoped keys:
      - `zootopia_tool_model:<sessionScopeKey>:<toolScopeId>`
    - Legacy unscoped tool-model keys are still read as fallback during migration:
      - `zootopia_tool_model:<toolScopeId>`
    - `AuthScopedDocumentBoundary` now clears both:
      - the shared in-memory document context
      - the in-memory AI response cache
      whenever the authenticated session scope changes.
    - `clearSessionState(...)` also clears the AI response cache on logout/reset.
  - TTL policy:
    - `AUTH_SESSION_NORMAL_TTL_SEC`
      - default `43200` seconds
    - `AUTH_SESSION_FAST_ACCESS_TTL_SEC`
      - default `21600` seconds
    - `AUTH_SESSION_ADMIN_TTL_SEC`
      - default `7200` seconds
    - `AUTH_SESSION_INVALIDATION_TTL_SEC`
      - default `86400` seconds
    - Fast Access TTL is additionally bounded by `temporaryAccessExpiresAt` when present so expired temporary access cannot be stretched by a longer generic TTL.
- Added / Removed Flows:
  - Added:
    - backend auth-session bootstrap/refresh/logout APIs
    - dedicated frontend per-mode session managers
    - auth-mode-aware admin route gating
    - auth-mode-aware document runtime keying
    - auth-mode-aware tool-model persistence
    - auth-session-scope rehydration from persisted browser snapshots
    - sibling auth-mode invalidation on replacement login
  - Removed / replaced:
    - implicit admin-route trust based only on `isAdmin`
    - reliance on legacy generic local-session keys
    - cross-mode reuse of unscoped tool-model local storage as the primary source of truth
- Migration Notes:
  - Legacy browser keys now cleared during auth boot / cleanup:
    - `zootopia_admin_session`
    - `zootopia_session_expiry`
  - Legacy unscoped tool-model keys remain readable as fallback so older persisted selections are not silently lost during first use after upgrade.
  - Stored auth snapshots are now upgraded into the new `restoring` flow and then normalized through the new server session model.
  - `.env.example` was updated with the new auth-session Redis/TTL settings so deployment configs can match the live architecture intentionally.
- Fallback Behavior:
  - Auth-session Redis now supports in-memory fallback only when:
    - `AUTH_SESSION_MEMORY_FALLBACK_ENABLED` is not disabled
    - and `NODE_ENV !== production`
  - Document runtime keeps its existing memory fallback behavior for local/dev/CI-safe execution.
  - Backend auth middleware still supports controlled auto-recovery from a valid Firebase token when the current Redis session is absent, but the new flow now:
    - rehydrates a richer namespaced session
    - invalidates sibling auth-mode scopes on replacement
    - and rejects admin-route access when the live auth mode is not `admin`
- Verification:
  - Passed targeted tests:
    - `node_modules\.bin\tsx.cmd --test tests\authSessionScoping.test.ts tests\modelRouting.test.ts`
    - `node_modules\.bin\tsx.cmd --test tests\documentPromptContextResolver.test.ts tests\documentCleanupCoordinator.test.ts`
    - `node_modules\.bin\tsx.cmd --test tests\documentRuntime.test.ts`
    - `node_modules\.bin\tsx.cmd tests\documentRuntimeSmoke.ts`
  - `npm run lint`
    - still fails because of pre-existing unrelated TypeScript issues outside this auth/session refactor, including existing errors in:
      - `server/adminAccountDirectoryService.ts`
      - `src/admin/components/CommunicationCenter.tsx`
      - `src/App.tsx`
      - `src/components/status/ResultPreviewContent.tsx`
      - `src/services/emailDeliveryService.ts`
      - `src/utils/exporters.ts`
      - `tests/adminAccountDirectoryService.test.ts`
    - The auth/session/document-runtime changes from this pass no longer appear in the remaining `tsc --noEmit` error list.

[2026-03-27] Layered Document Extraction Runtime Upgrade
- Area:
  - Document runtime extraction, shared prepared-document persistence, prompt-context resolution, and refresh-safe client rehydration.
- Files:
  - `server/documentRuntime/python/extract_document.py`
  - `server/documentRuntime/nativeExtractionService.ts`
  - `server/documentRuntime/ocrExtractionService.ts`
  - `server/documentRuntime/extractionCoordinator.ts`
  - `server/documentRuntime/fileTypeDetectionService.ts`
  - `server/documentRuntime/promptContextAssembler.ts`
  - `server/documentRuntime/documentIntakeService.ts`
  - `server/documentRuntime/pythonDocumentWorker.ts`
  - `src/ai/services/aiExecutor.ts`
  - `src/components/AuthScopedDocumentBoundary.tsx`
  - `src/contexts/DocumentContext.tsx`
  - `src/contexts/documentState.ts`
  - `src/services/documentRuntimeService.ts`
  - `tests/documentState.test.ts`
- Root Cause:
  - The Python extractor contract was too shallow and internally duplicated, which made extraction quality improvements hard to trust and hard for the TypeScript runtime to consume consistently.
  - Mixed PDFs could still miss OCR in practice because file-type strategy selection was based on whole-document density and frontend Gemini execution did not resolve the authoritative shared `documentContextRef`.
  - Refresh/reload recovery was incomplete because the in-memory document context treated the browser `File` object as a prerequisite for readiness even after a prepared artifact had already been persisted in the shared runtime.
- Summary:
  - Reworked the live Python extractor path into a richer layered contract that records extractor chains, fallback chains, warnings, page counts, text length, OCR usage, and per-unit metadata while keeping the existing runtime architecture intact.
  - Added a late PDF OCR fallback in the extraction coordinator so native-first PDFs with weak pages can still merge in OCR text safely instead of silently shipping sparse pages downstream.
  - Made frontend Gemini execution resolve prepared document context from `/api/documents/:documentId/context`, aligning frontend prompt assembly with the same shared prepared artifact used by backend `/api/ai/execute`.
  - Added refresh-safe active-document rehydration from `/api/documents/active` and updated document readiness rules so prepared documents remain `ready` without requiring the original browser `File`.
- Technical Details:
  - Python layered extractor:
    - `extract_document.py` now emits richer extraction payloads with:
      - `engine`
      - `pages`
      - `fullText`
      - `notes`
      - `warnings`
      - `extractorChain`
      - `fallbackChain`
      - `pageCount`
      - `textLength`
      - `metadata`
      - `ocrBlocks`
      - `ocrUsed`
    - PDF native extraction keeps explicit page numbering and records weak pages for later OCR decisions.
    - DOCX extraction walks the XML body in real author order so paragraphs and tables stay in logical sequence instead of being split into separate passes.
    - XLSX/CSV extraction stays sheet-aware, preserves sheet names and row order, and emits structured sheet blocks rather than a single raw grid dump.
    - PaddleOCR extraction records OCR block metadata, block confidence, page labels, and OCR warnings when no readable blocks are produced.
    - Docling is treated as a layout-aware supplement/fallback layer rather than a blind replacement:
      - preload when file type / mode makes sense
      - supplement weak native pages
      - fill OCR gaps
      - persist docling notes/warnings and extractor metadata
  - Fallback behavior:
    - `fileTypeDetectionService.ts` now tracks sparse PDF pages and biases those PDFs toward `pdf_hybrid_merge` even when total document coverage looks acceptable at a glance.
    - `extractionCoordinator.ts` adds a targeted late OCR pass for native-selected PDFs when Python/native metadata still reports weak pages.
    - Coordinator extraction metadata now stores:
      - `extractorChain`
      - `fallbackChain`
      - `warnings`
      - `qualitySignals`
      - `extractionDetails`
      - late PDF OCR attempt state
  - Runtime persistence:
    - `documentIntakeService.ts` now writes extractor-chain and fallback-chain slices into ready-state runtime metadata and logs richer persistence diagnostics on ready/cancel/fail.
    - Prepared artifacts still flow through the existing authoritative path:
      - intake API
      - extraction coordinator
      - document structure normalizer
      - artifact storage
      - artifact store
      - runtime active-document state
    - No parallel document runtime was introduced.
  - Prompt orchestration / tool consumption:
    - `promptContextAssembler.ts` now exposes extractor/fallback lineage inside assembled metadata and summary/insight strings so downstream tools can debug which layers produced the prepared text.
    - `aiExecutor.ts` now resolves `documentContextRef` through the shared backend prompt-context API before frontend Gemini orchestration, so tools such as quiz/study/chat paths can consume the same prepared extracted text instead of clipped local-only context.
  - Refresh / shared availability:
    - `documentRuntimeService.ts` now exposes `fetchDocumentPromptContext(...)`.
    - `AuthScopedDocumentBoundary.tsx` rehydrates the active prepared document from `/api/documents/active` when the auth-scoped React mirror is empty.
    - `documentState.ts` and `DocumentContext.tsx` now allow a prepared document to remain `ready` when it has persisted document identity plus extracted/context text, even if `file === null`.
- Observability:
  - Added/expanded structured logs for:
    - file-type detection
    - extraction completion
    - empty extraction failure
    - persistence-ready
    - persistence-cancelled
    - persistence-failed
  - Logged details now include page/section counts, weak PDF pages, OCR usage, extractor chain, fallback chain, warnings, and processing pathway.
- Verification:
  - Passed:
    - `python -m py_compile server\documentRuntime\python\extract_document.py`
    - direct Python extractor smoke on `sample.txt`, confirming the new native payload shape (`warnings`, `extractorChain`, `pageCount`, `textLength`, `metadata`, capabilities, attempted layers)
    - escalated TypeScript import smoke over changed runtime modules (`import-smoke-ok`)
    - escalated TypeScript behavior smoke covering:
      - prepared-document rehydration readiness without a browser `File`
      - prompt-context metadata propagation for extractor/fallback chains (`ts-smoke-ok`)
  - Incomplete / environment-limited:
    - `tsx --test` document-runtime suites could not complete within the available execution window after sandbox spawn restrictions were removed.
    - `tsc --noEmit` / repo `npm run lint` did not finish within the available timeout budget in this environment, so full-project typecheck confirmation remains outstanding.
- Notes:
  - The repository already contained unrelated modified files before/during this pass; this entry only covers the owner files listed above.
  - The requested `documentPromptContextResolver.ts` and `documentCleanupCoordinator.ts` owner names do not exist in this repo; the real live owners are `promptContextResolver.ts` and `cleanupCoordinator.ts`.

[2026-03-27]
- Area: Startup / Auth Bootstrap / Session Lifetime / Recovery Diagnostics
- Files: `/src/auth/AuthContext.tsx`, `/src/auth/hooks/useAuthActions.ts`, `/src/auth/session/sessionApi.ts`, `/src/auth/session/storage.ts`, `/src/components/ProtectedRoute.tsx`, `/src/App.tsx`, `/server/authSessionService.ts`, `/server.ts`, `/.env.example`, `/tests/authSessionLifetime.test.ts`, `/ZOOTOPIA_PROJECT_LEDGER.txt`
- Summary: Stabilized platform entry by replacing the split startup/auth/session restore flow with one authoritative bootstrap coordinator, fixing the async profile-sync retry bug that produced half-restored sessions, propagating typed session failures end to end, and enforcing a hard maximum 3-hour session lifetime for normal, fast-access, and admin sessions.
- Root Cause:
  - The visible `Startup is taking longer than expected` screen was mostly a false recovery trigger caused by a real orchestration bug, not just a cosmetic timeout.
  - `src/auth/AuthContext.tsx` treated `pendingFirebaseSession` as authenticated enough for route entry, so protected routes and admin routing could proceed before backend session validation and profile hydration were both complete.
  - `src/auth/hooks/useAuthActions.ts` used `setTimeout(...syncUserWithFirestore...)` retries that returned early instead of awaiting the retried work. That let callers continue as if profile sync had finished even while restore work was still pending or had silently failed.
  - Restore/login/bootstrap authority was split across:
    - Firebase `onAuthStateChanged`
    - frontend profile sync
    - backend `/api/auth/session/bootstrap`
    - route guards
    - ad-hoc recovery timers
  - Session lifetime enforcement was not anchored tightly enough to Firebase `auth_time`, so restore/refresh activity could continue around the intended maximum-lifetime policy.
- Safe Fix Implemented:
  - `src/auth/AuthContext.tsx`
    - introduced a stronger startup state model:
      - `bootstrapping`
      - `restoring`
      - `validating`
      - `hydrating_profile`
      - `authenticated`
      - `unauthenticated`
      - `expired`
      - `invalid`
      - `failed`
      - `logging_out`
    - removed optimistic `isAuthenticated` gating from `pendingFirebaseSession`
    - now unlocks routing only after the authoritative bootstrap barrier finishes
    - added a single retryable `runAuthoritativeBootstrap(...)` path used by:
      - login
      - identifier login
      - admin login
      - session restore
    - dedupes overlapping bootstrap attempts for the same Firebase user and guards against stale late completions
    - classifies recovery issues with explicit `reason` and `phase` metadata instead of showing a generic panic state without context
    - adds client-side hard-expiry handling that signs out and clears stale restore state exactly at session expiry instead of allowing half-dead sessions to drift
    - adds concise structured logs for:
      - startup begin
      - Firebase hydration resolved
      - backend bootstrap begin/end
      - workspace profile sync begin
      - bootstrap success/failure
      - hard expiry
      - retry/reset actions
  - `src/auth/hooks/useAuthActions.ts`
    - `syncUserWithFirestore(...)` now returns the synchronized `User` and no longer mutates auth state out of band
    - retry branches now `await` the next attempt instead of scheduling background retries and returning early
    - login/admin sign-in helpers no longer perform a second hidden auth bootstrap path; they defer to the authoritative `AuthContext` coordinator
  - `src/auth/session/sessionApi.ts`
    - added typed `AuthSessionApiError`
    - preserves backend error codes for:
      - `SESSION_EXPIRED`
      - `SESSION_MAX_LIFETIME_EXCEEDED`
      - `SESSION_INVALIDATED`
      - `SESSION_MISSING`
      - `AUTH_MODE_MISMATCH`
    - keeps bounded request timeouts for bootstrap / refresh / logout so real backend stalls surface deterministically instead of hanging the startup promise indefinitely
  - `src/auth/session/storage.ts`
    - stale/expired/invalid stored session snapshots are now pruned before restore
    - stale auth-mode hints are cleared when their matching stored snapshot is no longer usable
    - this prevents stale cross-mode browser persistence from re-entering bootstrap with an already-dead restore snapshot
  - `src/components/ProtectedRoute.tsx`
    - route protection now logs canonical gate outcomes:
      - waiting for bootstrap
      - redirect to login
      - admin mismatch
      - fast-access locks
      - startup recovery shown
      - allow
    - preserves existing role boundaries and route behavior while making the gating decision observable
  - `src/App.tsx`
    - login-route guard now logs final route resolution decisions for authenticated restores instead of leaving that step opaque
  - `server/authSessionService.ts`
    - added hard lifetime helpers anchored to Firebase `auth_time`
    - exported pure helpers for regression tests
    - session fingerprints now key on login-time identity (`auth_time`) instead of silent token refresh `iat`, preventing unnecessary session churn during ordinary token refreshes
    - `ensureMaximumLifetimeNotExceeded(...)` now rejects bootstrap/validation once the hard lifetime is over and invalidates the current server session as expired
    - invalidation now distinguishes:
      - `logging_out`
      - `expired`
      - `invalid`
    - `resolveSessionTtlSec(...)` now clamps fast-access sessions by both:
      - the 3-hour hard session maximum
      - `temporaryAccessExpiresAt` when the temporary window ends sooner
    - current-session refresh/touch keeps Redis TTL inside the remaining hard lifetime instead of extending it past the max window
  - `server.ts`
    - auth session endpoints now return structured auth-session errors through `sendAuthSessionError(...)`, preserving session error codes/state for the frontend bootstrap coordinator
  - `/.env.example`
    - documented `AUTH_SESSION_MAX_LIFETIME_SEC=10800`
    - set compatibility TTL examples for normal / fast_access / admin to 10800 so deployment defaults align with the new policy
  - `/tests/authSessionLifetime.test.ts`
    - added regression coverage for:
      - remaining hard lifetime
      - fast-access TTL clamp
      - session fingerprint stability across token refreshes
      - hard expiry detection after three hours
- TTL / Invalidation Rules Now Enforced:
  - Maximum session lifetime:
    - normal: hard max 3 hours
    - fast_access: hard max 3 hours, or earlier if `temporaryAccessExpiresAt` ends first
    - admin: hard max 3 hours
  - Lifetime anchor:
    - Firebase `auth_time` is authoritative
    - silent token refreshes do not reset the 3-hour window
  - Invalidation:
    - logout => `logging_out`
    - hard expiry / expired Redis snapshot => `expired`
    - mode mismatch / replaced / stale invalidation record => `invalid`
    - switching auth lanes still invalidates sibling mode sessions for the same uid
  - Startup recovery:
    - recovery UI now represents a failed authoritative bootstrap path
    - valid sessions no longer enter the platform on a speculative pending-Firebase-only state and then later panic into recovery

[2026-03-28]
- Area: Cloud Run Docker Build / Python Runtime Stability
- Files: /Dockerfile, /.dockerignore, /.gcloudignore, /ZOOTOPIA_PROJECT_LEDGER.txt
- Summary: Fixed the Cloud Run source-build failure by removing fragile version-interpolated Python package installs from the Dockerfile and aligning build-context ignores with the Python document-runtime workflow.
- Reason: Cloud Build was failing during `apt-get install` because `PYTHON_VERSION` was declared before `FROM` and therefore was not safely available inside the active build stage, causing package names like `python${PYTHON_VERSION}` to collapse incorrectly. The safest repo-specific fix was to install Debian bookworm's stable `python3` packages directly while preserving the existing Python 3.11 runtime contract and repo-local virtualenv execution path.
- Technical Details:
  - Updated `Dockerfile` to install `python3`, `python3-pip`, and `python3-venv` instead of `python${PYTHON_VERSION}`/`python${PYTHON_VERSION}-venv`, removing the stage-ARG expansion failure point during Cloud Run Docker builds.
  - Kept the backend document runtime contract intact by preserving `DOCUMENT_RUNTIME_PYTHON_EXECUTABLE=/app/.venv/bin/python` and continuing to create/install the repo-local `.venv` before the existing deployment verification and frontend build steps.
  - Preserved the current native dependency layer (`build-essential`, `libgomp1`, `libglib2.0-0`, `libgl1`, `ca-certificates`) because the current backend image still needs Node native builds and Python OCR/document packages.
  - Added Python cache exclusions (`__pycache__/`, `*.py[cod]`) to both `.dockerignore` and `.gcloudignore` so local Python artifacts do not pollute Docker or Cloud Run source build contexts.
- Risks / Dependencies:
  - This fix assumes the existing `node:22-bookworm-slim` base remains on Debian bookworm, where the stable `python3` packages resolve to the project's intended Python 3.11 line.
  - The authoritative Python-version contract is still carried by `deployment/runtime-manifest.json`, `.python-version`, and the venv runtime path; the Dockerfile change intentionally avoids altering those contracts.
  - Python package install/runtime behavior still depends on the pinned extraction stack in `server/documentRuntime/python/requirements.txt` and any first-run model asset downloads those libraries may perform outside the image build.
- Notes:
  - Preserved the current Cloud Run + Firebase Hosting deployment model, `server.ts` backend entry, `/api/*` route shape, document runtime wiring, and backend worker invocation flow.
  - Chose the least-complexity safe fix for this repo: repair the Docker installation layer without introducing deployment redesigns, backend logic changes, or broader refactors.

  - Repository-wide `npm run lint` still reports unrelated pre-existing TypeScript errors outside this scope (for example in `CommunicationCenter.tsx`, `App.tsx`, `ResultPreviewContent.tsx`, `emailDeliveryService.ts`, and `exporters.ts`); no new errors from the touched runtime files were surfaced in that run.
- Notes:
  - Preserved:
    - auth/session architecture
    - admin vs user vs fast-access separation
    - document runtime ownership and contracts
    - AI execution architecture and backend timeouts
    - Firebase Hosting rewrite model
    - local integrated workflow
  - Intentionally left untouched:
    - broad billing provider refactors
    - existing deployment manifest structure
    - unrelated admin/UI type errors already present in the repository
  - Verification:
    - `npm run lint` was run after the change set; it still fails only on unrelated pre-existing repository errors outside the touched runtime/config files.

[2026-03-29]
- Area: Local Upload/Auth Recovery Hardening
- Files: /src/auth/AuthContext.tsx, /src/utils/authHeaders.ts, /src/services/documentRuntimeService.ts, /src/features/assessment-tool/pages/AssessmentDashboard.tsx, /server.ts, /ZOOTOPIA_PROJECT_LEDGER.txt
- Summary: Fixed a local upload-triggered false logout/recovery bug by tightening auth-session refresh invalidation rules and adding targeted diagnostics across upload, document intake, and auth refresh paths.
- Reason: During real local use, selecting/uploading a file could trigger a focus/visibility re-entry refresh while the integrated runtime was busy. The frontend refresh path was incorrectly signing users out on transient timeout/session-worded errors instead of only on verified auth invalidation.
- Technical Details:
  - Root cause / exact failing stage:
    - `src/auth/AuthContext.tsx` re-entry refresh (`window.focus` / `visibilitychange`) called `refreshActiveAuthSession('refresh')` while upload/document intake was underway.
    - The refresh catch path treated any error message containing `session`, `sign in`, or `authentication` as a real invalid session.
    - Transient local failures such as `Session refresh timed out.` or `Missing authenticated session token.` could therefore trigger `signOut(auth)` + `clearSessionState(...)`.
    - After that false invalidation, `ProtectedRoute` redirected the user to `/login`, and the app could fall into the visible startup/error recovery surface instead of keeping the upload error localized.
  - Fix applied:
    - Replaced broad message-regex invalidation in `src/auth/AuthContext.tsx` with explicit refresh-failure classification.
    - Session clear/sign-out now occurs only for verified auth/session invalidation conditions:
      - `SESSION_EXPIRED`
      - `SESSION_MAX_LIFETIME_EXCEEDED`
      - `SESSION_INVALIDATED`
      - `SESSION_MISSING`
      - `AUTH_MODE_MISMATCH`
      - explicit `401` / `403` refresh responses
    - Transient/unverified refresh failures now preserve the active session and only record diagnostics instead of kicking the user to login.
  - Diagnostics added:
    - `src/auth/AuthContext.tsx`:
      - re-entry refresh trigger source (`focus` vs `visibilitychange`)
      - refresh failure disposition (`verified_invalid` vs transient preserve)
      - timeout budget in use
    - `src/utils/authHeaders.ts`:
      - bearer-header request / missing-token diagnostics without logging secrets
    - `src/services/documentRuntimeService.ts`:
      - intake request start / completion / failure logs
    - `src/features/assessment-tool/pages/AssessmentDashboard.tsx`:
      - upload start and preparation failure logs with auth/session snapshot
    - `server.ts`:
      - request-context auth rejection diagnostics
      - `/api/documents/intake` start / completion / failure diagnostics
- Risks / Dependencies:
  - Preserves backend-authenticated upload/document intake and does not weaken owner scoping or session security.
  - Focus/visibility re-entry refresh still runs by design; only the false-invalidating error handling was narrowed.
- Notes:
  - Preserved intentionally:
    - current login/session architecture
    - admin/user/fast-access separation
    - backend document-runtime authority and owner scoping
    - localized upload error handling in the dashboard workflow
  - Post-fix behavior:
    - upload/runtime failures stay on the current page
    - transient refresh failures no longer cause false logout
    - startup recovery is no longer used as a leaked upload/runtime failure surface for this path
  - Verification:
    - `npm run lint` was run after the fix.
    - New lint errors introduced by this change set were fixed.
    - Remaining `npm run lint` failures are unrelated pre-existing repository issues outside this task, including current errors in:
      - `src/admin/components/CommunicationCenter.tsx`
      - `src/App.tsx`
      - `src/components/status/ResultPreviewContent.tsx`
      - `src/services/emailDeliveryService.ts`
      - `src/utils/exporters.ts`
      - `tests/adminAccountDirectoryService.test.ts`

[2026-03-29]
- Area: Local Document Runtime Auth Recovery + Upload/Preparation UX Separation
- Files: /server.ts, /server/documentRuntime/documentArtifactStore.ts, /server/documentRuntime/documentIntakeService.ts, /src/services/documentRuntimeService.ts, /src/features/assessment-tool/pages/AssessmentDashboard.tsx, /src/upload/FileUploader.tsx, /src/utils/authHeaders.ts, /ZOOTOPIA_PROJECT_LEDGER.txt
- Summary: Fixed the local authenticated upload path so valid browser sessions are preserved during document intake, recoverable local Firebase Admin credential failures no longer surface as raw `16 UNAUTHENTICATED` document-preparation breaks, and the UI now separates file upload completion from later document preparation.
- Reason: In the local integrated runtime, the browser was already sending a valid bearer token for `POST /api/documents/intake`, but the backend could still hit recoverable Firebase Admin / Firestore credential failures while reading bootstrap user data or persisting document metadata. That caused the preparation step to fail even though the browser session remained valid. The frontend also blended upload and preparation into one blocking UX state, so users could not tell whether bytes upload had succeeded before preparation failed.
- Technical Details:
  - Exact failing request / stage:
    - The failing request is the follow-up authenticated intake request `POST /api/documents/intake`, not file selection itself.
    - Frontend token attachment path was preserved and remains lightweight:
      - `auth.currentUser?.getIdToken()` is still used without force-refresh in `src/utils/authHeaders.ts`
      - the document-intake request still requires bearer auth and backend owner scoping
    - Root local failure source:
      - recoverable Firebase Admin / Firestore credential errors during backend bootstrap user-data reads and/or document metadata persistence
      - these failures were leaking as raw `16 UNAUTHENTICATED: Request had invalid authentication credentials...` even though the browser session itself was still valid
  - Auth/session fix:
    - Added token-derived local fallback user-data resolution in `server.ts` for recoverable backend credential failures on normal-user flows while preserving:
      - admin separation
      - fast-access separation
      - backend token verification
      - auth-session validation boundaries
    - Fast-access fallback was intentionally not generalized from token-only data to avoid weakening expiry / scope enforcement.
  - Document runtime fix:
    - Added local-safe in-memory metadata fallback inside `server/documentRuntime/documentArtifactStore.ts` for recoverable Firebase Admin / Firestore credential failures.
    - The fallback only covers document-runtime metadata persistence/reads and mirrors the existing philosophy already used elsewhere in the repo for local Redis-optional development.
    - Owner-scoped file payloads, backend auth middleware, and runtime actor ownership checks remain in place.
    - Added targeted diagnostics for:
      - source-file persisted
      - document record ready
      - artifact record ready
      - artifact-store fallback activation / fallback reads/writes
  - Upload vs preparation UX separation:
    - Kept the existing `/api/documents/intake` contract intact.
    - Reworked `src/services/documentRuntimeService.ts` intake transport to use upload-progress-aware request handling so the UI can detect when file bytes are fully uploaded before the long-running preparation response returns.
    - Updated `src/features/assessment-tool/pages/AssessmentDashboard.tsx` stages to:
      - validate
      - upload
      - extract / prepare
      - store
      - ready
    - After bytes upload completes, the UI now marks the upload stage complete with a clear `File uploaded successfully` state, then automatically transitions into a separate preparation stage.
    - If preparation later fails, the completed upload stage remains visible instead of collapsing the whole flow into a generic upload failure.
    - Updated `src/upload/FileUploader.tsx` loading copy so the hero clearly distinguishes:
      - active upload
      - upload complete
      - later document preparation
  - Error handling improvements:
    - Added specific preparation-failure mapping for local backend credential rejection so this path is surfaced as a localized document-preparation/runtime issue instead of a misleading browser-auth/session invalidation issue.
    - Preparation failures now remain localized on the same page and do not imply the user was logged out.
  - Diagnostics added / refined:
    - `src/utils/authHeaders.ts`: token reuse source + current-user header-resolution diagnostics
    - `src/services/documentRuntimeService.ts`: request URL + upload/progress-aware intake diagnostics
    - `server/documentRuntime/documentIntakeService.ts`: source/document/artifact persistence stage diagnostics
    - `server/documentRuntime/documentArtifactStore.ts`: explicit fallback activation/read/write diagnostics for local credential recovery
- Risks / Dependencies:
  - Local document-runtime metadata fallback is intentionally development-oriented and memory-backed; it preserves the current local integrated workflow but is not a substitute for durable Firestore metadata in production.
  - Backend token verification and runtime ownership checks remain required; this change does not make document intake anonymous or bypass scoped access.
- Notes:
  - Preserved intentionally:
    - current login/session architecture
    - admin vs user vs fast-access separation
    - backend document-runtime ownership model
    - existing `/api/documents/intake` contract
    - current local integrated runtime model
  - Verification:
    - `npm run lint` passes successfully with `tsc --noEmit`.
    - Additional focused document-runtime verification:
      - `node_modules\\.bin\\tsx.cmd --test tests\\documentPromptContextResolver.test.ts tests\\documentCleanupCoordinator.test.ts` passed
      - `node_modules\\.bin\\tsx.cmd --test tests\\documentRuntime.test.ts` still fails due a pre-existing test-environment logger issue (`import.meta.env.DEV` is undefined in `src/utils/logger.ts` under that Node test path), not due to the document-intake/auth changes in this fix
